At the third level, your religious studies have taught you that in a challenge of the righteous and the sinful, the righteous will triumph. As an ability action, you issue a challenge that compels other creatures to do battle with you.
:
Pick one creature within sight. On a failed save, a creature can't willingly move away from you. Additionally, if the creature chooses to attack, they have disadvantage attacking anyone except you.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter V: Classes | War Priest }}

\page

:
You can only challenge one target a time - if you choose to challenge another creature while a second is currently under the effects of Challenge of the Righteous, all effects disappate. A creature can reroll the saving throw at the end of each of their turns.
:
When used outside of combat, on a failed save, the target will still suffer the above affects, but they will also attempt to initiate a duel.
:
This effect ends on the creature if you are incapacitated or die or if you lose sight of the creature.

#### Foresight of the Gods

At the fourth level, your connection with your god has grown stronger. When you take a rest, your dreams can take the form of powerful visions.
:
These visions are flashes of individual moments in the near future, and are usually focused on one specific person or object.

#### Extra Attack

At the fifth level, when you take the attack action you can make two attacks as part of one action. This ability does not stack with another “Extra Attack” class ability.

#### Aura of Leadership

At the sixth level, your religious teachings have given you insight into how to lead better. Choose one from the following auras:

##### Aura of Protection

Whenever you and a friendly creature within 10 feet of you must make a saving throw, the creature gains a bonus to half of your Paladin level. You must be conscious to grant this bonus.

##### Aura of Alacrity

Your presence invigorates your companaions, allowing them to push their bodies to farther limits. Your walking speed increases by 10 feet. In addition, if you aren't incapacitated, the walking speed of any ally who starts their turn within 5 feet of you increases by 10 feet until the end of that turn.

##### Aura of Courage

You and friendly creatures within 10 feet of you can't be frightened while you are conscious.

##### Aura of Hate

You and friendly creatures gain advantage when making a melee attack against an opponent affected by Challenge of the Righteous. On a hit, you deal extra damage equal to half of your Paladin level.
:
This burning hatred causes you and friendly creatures who use this ability to focus solely on the hated opponent, opening them up to strikes from other enemies. Attacks against you and friendly abilities using this ability gain advantage.

#### Divine Health

At the seventh level, the martial connection to your god makes your immune to disease and poison (damage).

#### Fruit of the Spirit

At the eighth level, you begin to heavily display one of the standard tenents your religions follow. Choose one of the following "fruits"; it should fit with the beliefs of your religion and god.

##### Dread

Your religion states that all should fear your god. Once per rest, you are able to display this dread to your enemies.
:
As shadows grow around you, make a Performance check constested against a Mental Fortitude Saving Throw from each creature of your choice that you can see. On a failure, the creature becomes Frightened of you until they exit combat. They gain no extra chances to remove this condition while in combat.

##### Faithfulness

Your religion holds that when you follow something, you should not waver in your beliefs. You gain advantage to Mental Fortitude checks and Saving Throws.

##### Joy

Your religion believes that a person's greatest happiness comes from their faith. You become immune to falling into despair or becoming Frightened. Allied creatures within 30 ft of you gain advantage to Saving Throws against becoming Frightened. Once per rest, you remember this joy, regaining hit points equal to twice your Paladin level.
:
If this total takes you over your maximum hit points, any extra hit points become temporary hit points. Any temporary hit points gained from this ability that are not lost during combat will be lost upon taking a rest.

##### Self Sacrifice

Your religion holds that a love of others is the most important attribute of someone. Once per round, when an allied creature is targetted from an attack, you can interpose yourself between the attacker and your ally. The attack roll is then made against your Armor Class, and if the attack hits, you take the damage. You must interpose before the LM states the attack roll.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter V: Classes | War Priest }}

\page

Additionally, you must have the movement range (subtracting movement already expended in this round of combat) to reach the point where you would interpose yourself. This ability does not count as a Reaction.
##### Suffering

Your religion holds that people only grow from suffering. Even if the suffering is moments before death, your religious tenants state that a person can take the knowledged gained from the experience into their afterlife. As a follower of your religion, it is your duty to inflict that suffering. Your crit range increases by 1 - if you have no other modifiers to you crit range, it would be 19-20. 

#### Relentless Avenger

At the ninth level, you feel anger and pain when your allies are attacked. As a reaction when an ally is attacked, you can immediately make an opportunity attack against this foe. You do not need to be adjacent to this enemy already, but they need to be within your movement range (subtracting movement already expended in this round of combat). The speed and ferocity of any movement you take as part of this reaction is too fast for opponents to make opportunity attacks.

#### Second Aura of Leadership

At the tenth level, you are able to choose another aura presented in the fourth level ability "Aura of Leadership". You cannot take an aura more than once.

#### Champion of the Gods

At the eleventh level, your martial prowess and dedication to your religious order has caught the eye of your god. The range of all auras you have increases to 30 feet, regardless of the original range, and you gain resistance to all non-magical damage.
:
Your companions have also grabbed the attention of your god, as the Companions of the Champion. While they are within 30 feet of you, they gain advantage on both Death Saving Throws and Mental Fortitude Saving Throws.

### Cleric (Magic)

**Skill Modifier Bonuses**: You gain a +2 bonus to **Tradition (of your religion)**.
:
You additionally gain as +1 increase to the skill modifier of 3 of the following skills. You cannot choose any skill more than once. **Insight**, **Intimidation**, **Medicine**, **Mental Fortitude**, **Persuasion**, **Perception**, **Reflex**
:
**Tool Modifier Bonuses**: You gain a +2 bonus to **Healer’s Kit**
:
**Weapon Modifier Bonuses**: You gain a +1 bonus to one weapon group of your choice
:
**Spellcasting Modifier Bonuses**: You gain a +2 modifier increase to two Schools of Magic of your choice, and an additional +1 modifier to 2 other schools of magic
:
**Armor Training**: You are trained with Light armor
:
**Shield Training**: You are not trained with Shields
:
**Starting Equipment**: 5d4 * 10 gold to spend on your starting equipment
:
**Health**: At the first level, you start with 11 + your Constitution Modifier hit points, and gain the same amount upon a level up.
:
**Primary Spellcasting Skill**: Tradition (of your religion)
:
**Mana**: At the first level, you start with 11 + your Tradition (of your religion) Modifier mana.
:
Upon a level up, you gain mana equal to your Tradition (of your religion) Modifier.
:
**Number of Spells Known**: At the first level, you know 4 + your Tradition (of your religion) Modifier spells.
:
Upon a level up, you learn 1 spell. Whenever your Tradition (of your religion) Modifier increases, you learn an additional spell.

| Level | Feature Gained |
|:-----:|:--------------:|
| 1 | Thaumaturgy |
| 2 | Disciple of Life |
| 3 | Channel Divinity |
| 4 | Spellcasting Specialization |
| 5 | Arcane Recovery |
| 6 | Second Channel Divinity |
| 7 | Divine Smite |
| 8 | Channel Divinity: Aura of Healing |
| 9 | Spellcasting Smite |
| 10 | Supreme Healing |
| 11 | Divine Intervention |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter V: Classes | War Priest }}

\page

#### Thaumaturgy

At the first level, you can manifest a minor wonder, a sign of supernatural power, within range. You create one of the following magical effects within range:

 - Your voice booms up to three times as loud as normal for 1 minute.
 - You cause flames to flicker, brighten, dim, or change color for 1 minute.
 - You cause harmless tremors in the ground for 1 minute.
 - You create an instantaneous sound that originates from a point of your choice within range, such as a rumble of thunder, the cry of a raven, or ominous whispers.
 - You instantaneously cause an unlocked door or window to fly open or slam shut.
 - You alter the appearance of your eyes for 1 minute.

:
If you cast this spell multiple times, you can have up to three of its 1-minute effects active at a time, and you can dismiss such an effect as an action.

#### Disciple of Life

At the second level, your healing spells are more effective. Whenever you cast a spell to restore hit points to a creature, the creature regains additional hit points equal to 2 + your Tradition (of your religion) modifier.

#### Channel Divinity

At the third level, you gain use of one of the Channel Divinities presented below; it should fit with the beliefs of your religion and god. You can use your Channel Divinity a number of times equal to your Cleric level per rest.

##### Balm of Peace

You can use your Channel Divinity to make your very presence a soothing balm. As an action, you can move up to your speed, without provoking opportunity attacks, and when you move within 5 feet of any other creature during this action, you can restore a number of hit points to that creature equal to 2d6 + your Tradition (of your religion) modifier. A creature can receive this healing only once whenever you take this action.

##### Knowledge of the Ages

You can use your Channel Divinity to tap into a divine well of knowledge. As an action, you choose one skill or tool. For 10 minutes, you add +10 to checks or saving throws with that skill or tool.

##### Path to the Grave

You can use your Channel Divinity to mark another creature's life force for termination.
:
As an action, you choose one creature you can see within 30 feet of you, cursing it until the end of your next turn. The next time you or an ally of yours hits the cursed creature with an attack, the creature has vulnerability to all of that attack's damage, and then the curse ends.

##### Preserve Life

You can use your Channel Divinity to heal the badly injured.
:
As an action, you present your holy symbol and evoke healing energy that can restore a number of hit points equal to five times your Cleric level. Choose any creatures within 30 feet of you, and divide those hit points among them. This feature can restore a creature to no more than half of its hit point maximum. You can't use this feature on an undead or a construct.

##### Touch of Death

You can use Channel Divinity to destroy another creature's life force by touch. When you creature with a melee attack, you can use Channel Divinity to deal extra necrotic damage to the target. The damage equals 5 + twice your Cleric level.

#### Spellcasting Specialization

At the fourth level, you can choose a school of magic specialisation from the following options.

##### Abjuration

You have been trained with an emphasis on casting Abjuration spells. When casting Abjuration spells, you gain a +1 bonus to your Abjuration Spellcasting Modifier.

##### Divination

You have been trained with an emphasis on casting Divination spells. When casting Divination spells, you gain a +1 bonus to your Divination Spellcasting Modifier.

##### Necromancy

You have been trained with an emphasis on casting Necromancy spells. When casting Necromancy spells, you gain a +1 bonus to your Necromancy Spellcasting Modifier.

#### Arcane Recovery

At the fifth level, your connection to magic gross stronger. After completion of a rest, you regain an additional amount of mana equal to your Cleric level.

#### Second Channel Divinity

At the sixth level, you gain a second Channel Divinity as presented in the third level ability "Channel Divinity". You cannot choose the same Channel Divinity more than once.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter V: Classes | War Priest }}

\page


#### Divine Smite

At the seventh level, when you hit a creature with a weapon attack, you can expend 2 Mana to deal an extra 1d8 radiant damage to the target.

#### Channel Divinity: Aura of Healing

As an action, you can expend one of your Channel Divinity usages to heal yourself and all friendly creatures within 30 feet of you. All affected creatures regain hit points equal to your Tradition (of your religion) modifier. This healing is not affected by Disciple of Life.

#### Spellcasting Smite

At the ninth level, your Divine Smite extends to your spell attacks. When you cast a spell that deals damage, you can expend 2 Mana to deal an extra 1d8 radiant damage to the target.

#### Supreme Healing

Starting at tenth level, when you would normally roll one or more dice to restore hit points with a spell, you instead use the highest number possible for each die. For example, instead of restoring 2d6 hit points to a creature, you restore 12.

#### Divine Intervention

At the eleventh level, you can call on your deity to intervene on your behalf when your need is great.
:
Imploring your deity's aid requires you to use your action. Describe the assistance you seek. The LM chooses the nature of the intervention; the effect of any cleric spell or cleric feature would be appropriate. You can use this ability once per 7 days.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter V: Classes | War Priest }}

\page

## Multiclassing

As hinted in the chapter overview, having a character multiclass is possible. However, there are a few restrictions.
:
In order to multiclass into another class's archetype that matches your primary one, you must have more levels in your primary class than what you are multiclassing into. If you are a level 1 Novitiate with one level in Fighter, you can multiclass into any other class' martial archetype, such as Artisan's Craftsmen. When leveling up to level 3, assuming you took the level 1 Craftsmen feature as your level 2 bonus, you can multiclass into another class' martial archetype that is not Artisan, or you can take the second level Fighter feature.
:
You cannot take the level two Craftsmen feature, because then your number of levels in Craftsmen would outweight your number of levels in Fighter.
:
It is not considered multiclassing to take levels in your class's opposite archetype - a level 1 Novitiate with one level in Fighter can take their level 2 increase in Wizard. However, with subsequent level ups, you must take a second level in Fighter prior to levelling up Wizard. Your number of levels in your primary archetype must be equal to or greater than the number of levels in the other.
:
Finally, when multiclassing into another class' opposite archetype, your primary class' opposite archetype must be at an equal or higher level than the second class'. For instance, say that a character started off as a level 1 Novitiate (Fighter). They could not multiclass into Artisan (Artificier) until level 4.
:
Novitiate (Fighter) 1 + Artisan (Artificier) 1 doesn't work as the character's Novitiate (Wizard) level is not equal to or greater than Artisan (Artificier) 1.
:
Novitiate (Fighter) 1 + Novitiate (Wizard) 1 + Artisan (Artificier) 1 doesn't work as the character's Magic archetype's level is greater than the character's Martial archetype (which is their primary).
:
This character would need to be Novitiate (Fighter) 2 + Novitiate (Wizard) 1 in order to take a level in Artisan (Artificier).

### Features Gained

When you first multiclass into another class or take the first level in your classes' opposite Archetype , you do not gain any of the modifiers shown under **Skill Modifier Bonuses**, **Tool Modifier Bonuses**, **Weapon Modifier Bonuses**, or **Starting Equipment**. For **Armor Training**, you only gain training with Light Armor, if the class you are multiclassing into has it, and Shields.
:
For **Mana** and **Number of Spells Known**, if this is the first level in your classes' opposite archetype, you gain the first level increases. Otherwise, you take the level up bonuses.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter V: Classes | Multiclassing }}

\page

# Chapter VI: Equipment
For some players, the most exciting thing about character creation is considering how they act in combat; what armor will they be wearing? What weapon(s) will they have? Will they be a knight, wielding a sword and board, or will they be a classic barbarian, running around with no armor and a great axe?
:
In Natural Progressions, weapons and tools function just like skills - the modifier used is increased on a roll of a natural 20 and they have a maximum of 11, assuming no variant rules are used.
:
Weapons are grouped by categories. For example, when rolling a natural 20 when wielding a dagger, your **Dueling Blades** modifier increases by 1.
:
Rather than having a distinct armor or shield modifier like with weapons, both armor and shields add to a character's armor class, which is calculated as follows:
:
10 + armor bonus + weapon bonus + shield bonus + reflex skill modifier

## Weapons
This section details the weapons that are available to be used in Natural Progressions. First weapon properties will be defined, followed by the weapons themselves.
:
To give the feeling of progressing as a character gets better with a weapon, the traits and damage of weapons change depending on your weapon modifier - this is unique to each weapon (although bonuses may be given to a group of weapons, such as all Ambush Weapons).
:
The ability level is as follows:

0-1: **Untrained**

2-4: **Trained** 

5-8: **Experienced**

9-10: **Expert**

11: **Master** (with additionally perk)
:
Experienced, Expert and Master all have level requirements in order to use. A character's modifier can increase up to 11 without hitting the requirements, but their ability level will remain at Trained unless they hit the requirements.
:
**Experienced**: 2 levels in any Martial archetype. These levels can be split in any way among the Martial archetypes.
:
**Expert**: 6 levels in any Martial archetype. 2 of these levels must be within the same archetype.
:
**Master**: 11 levels in any Martial archetype. 5 of these levels must be within the same archetype.
:
Additionally, some abilities granted by weapons have a weapon DC, which is 10 + your weapon ability modifier.

### Improvised Weapons

Theoretically, just about anything can be considered a weapon with enough force - a rock, a bottle, even a pin. However, they generally are not nearly as effective as actual weapons.
:
With no abilities and features that affect improvised weapons, you use your Athletics modifier when determining if the attack hits. Upon a successful attack, you deal 1 damage of a type that makes sense. Generally it will be bludgeoning damage.

### Weapon Properties
Each combination of weapon and ability level has a set of properties that define what a weapon can and cannot do.

#### Affixed
This equipment is worn and wielded in the main or off hand. While dual wielding with an affixed weapon, the other weapon does not need the Light property. Affixed weapons are donned or doffed as an action and cannot be disarmed. While worn, it can be equipped for free during your turn, and while not equipped, it remains attached to your body, leaving your hand open for other things.

{{note
##### Reduced Weapon List
The number of weapons can make choosing a starting weapon(s) daunting. For games where players wish to have a reduced number of weapons to choose from, the following alternate choices are suggested:

**Ambush Weapons**: Guantlet, Unarmed Strike

**Axes**: Great Axe, Hand Axe

**Bludgeons**: Heavy Club, Morningstar, Quarterstaff

**Bows and Slings**: Longbow, Shortbow, Sling

**Combat Blades**: Broadsword, Longsword

**Crossbows**: Hand Crossbow, Heavy Crossbow, Light Crossbow

**Dueling Blades**: Dagger, Shortsword

**Flails and Whips**: Light Flail, Heavy Flail

**Hammers and Picks**: Light Hammer, Light Pick, War Hammer

**Polearms**: Bladed Staff, Glaive

**Spears**: Javelin, Pike, War Spear

**Throwing Weapons**: Dart, Throwing Knife

**Natural Weapons**: All
}}

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Overview }}

\page

#### Awkward
You do not have adequate training or experience to weird this weapon effectively, but you can still use it. You do not add your weapon skill bonus while rolling an attack or damage with this weapon.

#### Barbed
When this weapon is entangling your enemy, and the enemy succeeds on the check to escape from your grapple, that enemy takes your weapon's damage.

#### Balanced
When this weapon rolls a 1 on any of its damage dice, you may reroll that dice but must use the new result. If you wield this weapon with two hands, you may reroll the damage dice if it is a 1 or a 2.

#### Brace
As an action you choose to Brace. On your turn, choose any targets you can see that are more than 20 feet away from you. If any of those targets move within your weapon’s reach before your next turn, as a reaction you can roll one melee attack against them with advantage. If the attack hits, treat the attack as a critical hit. While bracing, if you use a different reaction, or move or get moved, you are no longer bracing. A brace attack is not an opportunity attack.

#### Conceal
At the start of combat, if your passive Sleight of Hand is higher than your enemy's passive perception, or as a bonus action make a Sleight of Hand check to beat this score, you can hide these weapons from your enemy. If hidden, the first attack made with it against a single unaware enemy is treated as attacking a Stunned creature, as your enemy wasn't expecting your weapon. Once you use the weapon, you cannot hide it again, nor can you make any further surprise attacks with any conceal weapon during that same encounter.

#### Deflect
When struck by a melee weapon attack, you can use your reaction to deflect some damage you would receive. If wielding one Deflect weapon, you may roll your weapon's standard damage dice (as defined by the weapon definition in this chapter), then subtract that total from the damage you would receive from a source you can see. If you are wielding a Deflect weapon with two hands, you can roll your weapon's damage dice twice. If you are wielding two deflect weapons, you can roll both weapon's deflect rolls and choose the highest result or you can choose to deflect another attack using your off hand weapon, as part of the same reaction. For the off hand deflect, you only deflect half of the damage on the dice roll.

Deflect does not interact with any other weapon property, such as keen or puncture; you simply roll your weapon's damage dice normally.

#### Disarm
When you hit with a Disarm attack, you deal damage equal to your weapon damage modifier, and force your enemy to roll its choice of an Athletics or Reflex Saving Throw. On a failure, it drops one held object of your choice, landing within 5ft of it in a direction of your choosing. If you have a free hand, you may come into possession of the disarmed object.

If your target is a category size larger than you or using a two-handed weapon, it gains advantage on this save, while enemies two size categories larger than you are immune to this attack from you. If it is smaller than you, it suffers disadvantage. If you land a critical hit with this attack, your weapon deals normal, non-critical damage in addition to forcing your enemy to roll the saving throw.

#### Double Ended
When you take the attack action, you can make one additional attack as an ability action using the damage listed - note that you do not add your weapon ability modifier for the offhand attack - if you are within 5 ft of your target and wielding your weapon with two hands.

#### Entangle
When you hit with an Entangle attack, you deal only your weapon ability modifier, and force the enemy to succeed on its choice of an Athletics or Reflex Saving Throw or be Restrained by you. To escape, the creature must succeed a grapple check against your weapon DC, gaining advantage if it is a size category larger than you. If you land a critical hit, your weapon deals normal, non-critical damage in addition to forcing your enemy to roll the saving throw. Creatures two size categories larger than you are immune to Entangle attacks from you.
:
While you are holding the weapon entangling your target, your weapon attacks against it automatically hit, but only deal damage equal to your weapon ability modifier. You can release an entangled enemy at any time. If you drop the weapon, the creature is immediately free.

#### Heavy
Category size Small creatures suffer disadvantage to attack rolls and Tiny and smaller cannot wield this weapon.

#### Hipshot
This ranged weapon is extremely nimble and maneuverable. When you make a ranged weapon attack, you ignore the disadvantage from a hostile creature within 5ft of you.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Overview }}

\page

#### Keen
This weapon is extraordinarily sharp or devastatingly accurate. When you score a critical hit with this weapon, add an additional damage dice to the weapon damage dice rolled. The added damage dice is not doubled from a critical hit.

#### Knockback
When you hit with a knockback attack, you deal only your weapon ability modifier, and your enemy must succeed on its choice of an Athletics or Reflex Saving Throw or be pushed 5 feet in a direction of your choosing. If you land a critical hit, your weapon deals normal, non-critical damage in addition to forcing your enemy to roll the saving throw. Creatures a size category larger than you gain advantage on this save. Creatures two sizes larger than you are immune to being pushed this way.

#### Light
In order to dual wield two weapons, both weapons you wield must have this property. You can make an attack with your off-hand weapon as a bonus action, but don't add any ability modifier to damage. There is no requirement that your off hand weapon be melee in order to dual wield.

#### Lunge
If you use an attack action, you can use 5ft of movement to attack a foe up to 5ft further than normal. Each attack which uses this property costs 5ft of movement. In order to use the lunge property, there must be clear ground in the direction of your lunge. You cannot lunge if an enemy or obstacle is directly in front of you.

#### Melee
Melee weapons make a melee weapon attack at a target up to 5ft away.

#### Natural
A natural weapon is one which is part of a creature's anatomy, such as teeth and claws. To have a natural weapon, you must either become a creature for which a natural weapon is listed in its stat block, or have a racial ability which allows you to make an attack using claws, teeth, etc in place of an unarmed attack. Natural weapons cannot be removed, disarmed, or broken in any way and are always equipped.

#### Nimble
When you make an attack against a creature that you are restraining or that you are restrained by, or while prone, you gain advantage
to the roll. This advantage does not cancel the disadvantage that may be appled by restraining or being restrained. It replaces it.

#### One Handed
This weapon requires only one hand to wield properly.

#### Penetrate
When you attack an enemy wearing armor, you ignore half of their armor bonus to their Armor Class.

#### Puncture
These piercing weapons deal significantly more damage if they hit a vital weak spot in the enemy. When you roll a maximum value with any of your weapon's damage dice, you can roll that dice again and add the result to the total damage dealt. This can keep happening as many times as you roll maximum values on damage dice, even on the new rolls.

#### Ranged
Ranged weapons make a ranged weapon attack within range. It must be loaded with ammunition to make an attack. The ranged numbers list its normal and maximum range. When attacking enemies beyond the normal range or with an enemy within 5ft of you, you suffer disadvantage for that attack. A ranged weapon cannot attack targets beyond its maximum range.

#### Reach
This weapon adds 5 feet to your reach when you make a melee weapon attack, as well as for determining your reach for opportunity attacks with it. Note that if there is a creature between you and your enemy within reach, your enemy has cover. Reach cannot be used to extend the range of a Double Ended attack.

#### Reload
Some ranged weapons take a time to reload, expressed in types of game actions. These game actions represent the time it takes to reset a weapon and prime it for another attack. From fastest to slowest, these are; free, reaction, ability, attack, action.
:
Reload weapons require two hands to reload unless otherwise stated. If dual wielding with a Reload weapon, one item must be sheathed or dropped to Reload.
:
Reloading as an action means that you must use your action in order to reload your weapon
:
Reloading as attack means you use an attack action and one of your main hand attacks is used to reload. If you have 3 attacks, you attack once, use your second attack to reload, then attack again. Note that you must use either an attack or an action to reload, and if you do not wish to attack, then reloading your weapon takes an action.
:
Reloading as an ability means that your must use you ability action to reload your weapon.
:
Likewise, reloading as a reaction means that you must use your reaction to reload your weapon.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Overview }}

\page

Reload free has no action economy cost and reloads as quickly as a bow. The only detriment is that a Reload weapon still takes two hands to reload.
:
You must always reload your weapon before using it for a ranged weapon attack again. If your weapon is empty at the end of your turn, it must be reloaded before you can use it again.
:
You have the choice of reloading your weapon with any of the options that are slower.

#### Thrown
Thrown weapons are used to make a ranged weapon attack by throwing them at the enemy, dealing their melee damage on hit unless a different damage value is listed after the Thrown weapon property.
:
You may draw and throw a weapon as part of the attack. If you throw a weapon without the Thrown property, the weapon is treated as an improvised weapon and may only cause a small amount of damage.

#### Trip
When you hit with a trip attack, you deal only your weapon ability modifier in damage on hit, and your enemy must succeed on its choice of an Athletics or Reflex Saving Throw or be knocked prone. If you land a critical hit, your weapon deals normal, non-critical damage in addition to forcing your enemy to roll the saving throw. Enemies a size category larger than you gain advantage on this save. Enemies two size categories larger than you are immune to being tripped in this way.

#### Two Handed
This weapon requires two hands to use when you attack with it. You can't use only one hand to attack with a two handed weapon.

#### Versatile
This weapon may be used with one or two hands and you can switch between them at any time. When used with two hands, you use the damage dice listed in parentheses.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Weapon Properties }}

\page

{{wide
### Ambush Weapons
| Weapon | Damage Types | Untrained Damage | Trained Damage | Experience Damage | Expert Damage | Master Damage | Weight | Cost |
|:-------|:------------:|:----------------:|:--------------:|:-----------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|:------:|:----:|
| Gauntlet | Bludgeoning, Piercing, or Slashing | 1d4 | 1d6 | 1d6 | 1d6 | 1d8 | 1 | 50 |
| Hidden Blade | Piercing | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1 | 10 |
| Interceptor | [None] | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 0 | 1 | 3 |
| Katar | Piercing or Slashing | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d6 | 1 | 5 |
| Knuckle Axe | Piercing or Slashing | 1d4 | 1d6 | 1d6 | 1d6 | 1d6 | 1 | 25 |
| Punch Dagger | Piercing or Slashing | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 0.5 | 1 |
| Side Baton | Bludgeoning | 1d4 | 1d6 | 1d6 | 1d6 | 1d8 | 2 | 10 |
| Unarmed Strike | Bludgeoning | 1d1 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d6 | 0 | 0 |
| Whip Dagger | Piercing | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 1d4 | 2 | 15 |
}}

#### Gauntlet

Spiked or weighted knuckles worn as a glove or held in hand. The hand with the gauntlet cannot be used to wield other equipment.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Affixed |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Affixed, Deflect, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Affixed, Deflect, Light, Nimble |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Affixed, Deflect, Disarm, Light, Nimble |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Affixed, Deflect, Disarm, Light, Nimble |
| Master Ability | When hit with a melee attack, as a reaction before the damage, you can attempt a disarm attack. If your enemy fails, you disarm them and take no damage. |

#### Hidden Blade

A mechanical means to instantly deploy a piercing dagger from under the wrist built into a bracer. The master takes full advantage of a surprise attack, ending a life in an instant.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Affixed, Conceal, Light |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Affixed, Conceal, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Affixed, Conceal, Light, Nimble |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Affixed, Conceal, Light, Nimble |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Affixed, Conceal, Light, Nimble |
| Master Ability | Surprised creatures take maximum damage from this weapon. |

\column

#### Interceptor

A generic term for clothing used to deflect, such as a thick wool cloak, silk scarf, or wide brimmed hat. While you may wear an interceptor, it must be equipped to be used but gives you +1 weapon AC when equipped. The master can catch missile weapons in flight, even protecting an ally.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | You cannot wield an intercepter without training |
| Trained    | One Handed, Affixed, Conceal, Deflect (d4), Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Affixed, Conceal, Deflect (d6), Disarm, Light |
| Expert     | One Handed, Affixed, Conceal, Deflect (d6), Disarm, Entangle, Light |
| Master     | One Handed, Affixed, Conceal, Deflect (d8), Disarm, Entangle, Light, Trip |
| Master Ability | Your deflect can be used against ranged weapon attacks. When a creature you can see attacks a target within 5 ft of you (yourself included), you can use your reaction to decrease the damage taken. |

#### Katar

A wide, leaf shaped blade mounted in line with the fist at the end of an H shaped handle. The katar is a unique punch weapon, and the master's speed and precision is unmatched.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Conceal, Light |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Nimble |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Keen, Light, Nimble |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Keen, Light, Nimble |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit, you can make an additional attack as part of this same action. These extra attacks can also activate this ability, but only on a natural 20. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Ambush Weapons }}

\page

#### Knuckle Axe

The knuckle axe resembles an axe head with no handle, and either 4 finger holes or a curved handle to rest inside a closed fist. Masters with knuckle axes slash through soft targets much like a real axe, attacking two targets at once.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Keen, Light |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Keen, Light |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Keen, Light |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit or reduce a target to 0hp, you may make an additional melee attack to another creature adjacent to you as part of the same action. |

#### Punch Dagger

A small knife attached to a horizontal handle that projects out from the fist when held. It can be easily deployed in a swift punching motion allowing a master true speed and precision unmatched.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Conceal, Light |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Nimble |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Nimble, Puncture |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Nimble, Puncture |
| Master Ability | You have advantage on attacks made outside of your turn. Additionally, if this weapon is in your off hand, you may make an opportunity attack with your main hand and this weapon. |

#### Side Baton

Often called a Tonfa, Riot Baton, or Arm Club, this defensive weapon is designed to deflect attacks with the forearm. It is a stout club with a perpendicular handle attached a third of the way down the length, allowing it to be swung out for a swipe, or extend the reach of a thrust. A master uses the handle as a hook just effectively as an axe and maximizes the defensive properties of this weapon.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Light |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Light, Trip |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Light, Trip |
| Master Ability | You gain +1 weapon AC. Your deflect roll is d10, rather than d8. |

#### Unarmed Strike

Untrained unarmed strikes are simple punches while training teaches proper punches and kicks. However, a real master of unarmed strikes is as well trained as a traditional monk.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Nimble |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Nimble |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Disarm, Nimble |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Disarm, Light, Nimble, Trip |
| Master Ability | You may make an Unarmed strike as an off hand attack even if you're wielding a weapon without the light property. You may spend an ability action to shove or perform a disarm attack. |

#### Whip Dagger

A dagger with a ring pommel at the end of a silk ribbon. The weapon can be used like a dagger in hand to attack creatures up to 5ft away, or swung about the end of the ribbon to attack creatures up to 10ft away. A master can perform the Scorpion Pull, an ability to impale a target and pull them closer with the attached ribbon.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Conceal, Reach |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Conceal, Reach |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Conceal, Entangle, Reach |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Conceal, Entangle, Lunge, Reach |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Conceal, Entangle, Lunge, Reach |
| Master Ability | When your attack is successful, as an ability action, you can choose to force the enemy to succeed on an Athletics check or be pulled up to 10ft toward you. You may only do this if your target is no more than 1 size category larger than you. |

#### Battle Axe

An axe about 2ft-3ft in length, with a longer beard designed for a wider slashing wound. This weapon is large enough to use with two hands for more powerful strikes, yet nimble enough to be used in one hand. Masters with the battle axe are stout and reliable with their bit, and throw the axe with a large overhand pitch with both hands at the base of the handle.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Versatile 1d10 |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Versatile 1d10 |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Trip, Versatile 1d10 |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Trip, Versatile 1d12 |
| Master Ability | You may reroll any result of 1 or 2 on any damage die caused by this weapon. If you are wielding the Battle Axe with two hands, it gains Thrown d12 (20/60). |

#### Greataxe

The classic barbarian axe, but which also includes more historical versions such as the bardiche, voulge, or Dane axe. The greataxe has incredible potential for damage, and the master greataxe wielder fells even the stoutest of foes with reliability not seen in many other weapon styles.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Reach |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Brace, Heavy, Reach |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Brace, Entangle, Heavy, Reach, Trip |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Brace, Heavy, Reach, Trip |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit you can roll all damage twice and take the better result. |

\column

#### Halberd

An axe blade topped with a spike mounted on an 8ft long shaft, with a hook on the back side of the axe blade for pulling mounted combatants from the saddle. With some experience, a halberd can be used to perform a trip against mounted foes to pull them from the saddle to a prone position, and the master has conquered this maneuver.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Trip |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Knockback, Trip |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Knockback, Trip |
| Master Ability | Your trip attacks impose disadvantage to checks made to resist them. |

#### Handaxe

An incredibly versatile weapon and tool, the hand axe can be thrown, or used in melee, and can be used to trip your foe, and the master binds and disarms with lightning efficiency. If you have a handaxe on your person, you may gain advantage on survival checks where the handaxe can be used to help, such as cutting firewood or putting up tents.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Thrown (10/30) |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Thrown (20/60) |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (20/60), Trip |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Light, Thrown (20/60), Trip |
| Master Ability | 	If you miss with a disarm attack, you may reroll but must take the new result. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Axes }}

\page

#### Hook Sword

An exotic weapon made famous by the northern Chinese masters; a shortsword length weapon in which the tip forms a prominent hook, and which the knuckle guard features a crescent shaped blade. A hook sword can easily catch weapons and limbs, giving it superior control over an enemy's movements.
:
The master can also join two hook swords together for a unique means of trapping and binding enemies, as well as striking further by forming a makeshift flail; letting go of one hook sword and swinging it by the hook of the other sword. Hooking the swords together, or unhooking and wielding them separately can be taken as part of an attack. When you hook two hook swords together, your weapon gains Reach and loses Light. While wielded in this way, your hook swords count as one weapon instead of dual wielding two weapons.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Entangle, Light |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Disarm, Entangle, Light |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Disarm, Entangle, Light, Trip |
| Master Ability | When you are hit with a melee weapon attack, as a reaction you can make a disarm or entangle attack against that enemy. |

#### Khopesh

This hybrid axe and sword was made famous by ancient Egyptians. It is a sword built with a large crescent shaped protrusion about one third from the tip, and a hooked tip, forming a sort of question mark shape. It acts similarly to a handaxe, but is lighter and can more reliably cut with a larger surface area. A Master with the Khopesh has learned to use the hooked point to hamstring enemies with ease.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Keen, Light |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Keen, Light |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Keen, Light, Trip |
| Master Ability | If you hit with a trip attack, your enemy's speed is reduced by 10ft until the end of their next turn. While they have this penalty, they suffer disadvantage to Athletic checks. |

\column

#### Poleaxe

An infantry weapon designed for use against armored foes, characterized by an axe on one side and a hammer on the other, tipped with a dagger-like spike from the top. It is typically on a 6 ft haft, shod with iron to protect it from damage. Though not long enough for a reach weapon, its style resembles that of a quarterstaff and axe combined. A master uses the weapon's iron shodding more actively, blocking attacks that would normally chop through the wood shaft.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Puncture |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Brace, Heavy, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Brace, Deflect, Heavy, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Brace, Deflect, Heavy, Penetrate, Puncture, Trip |
| Master Ability | You gain +1 weapon AC and you may add your weapon ability bonus to deflect rolls. |

#### Tomahawk

Also called a fransisca, this small axe features a slimmer blade more balanced for throwing, and an opposing spike or small hammer so both sides of the weapon were dangerous in flight.
:
Tomahawks are balanced for throwing further distances than any other axe, and the master throws them with great force, using the hammer or spike's weight to drive the thinner axe head deeper into a target and throw them off balance or strike their arm mid swing.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Thrown (10/30) |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Thrown (20/60) |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (40/120), Trip |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Disarm, Light, Thrown (40/120), Trip |
| Master Ability | If you score a critical hit, your enemy has disadvantage on its next attack roll. |

#### Bar Mace

A stout, arm length iron bar lined with spikes or flanges, more able to utilize prying leverage to deal with armored foes. Designed for low skilled military soldiers, a master uses the many angles to pry weapons from the enemy's hands.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Disarm |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Disarm |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Disarm |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit, you can choose to deal damage equal to your weapon ability modifier, but force your enemy to suffer disadvantage to attacks. At the end of their turn they can roll a Constitution check, ending this penalty on success. |

#### Bo Staff

The Japanese bo is a much smaller and thinner version of the quarterstaff, and the result is a much faster fighting style, devoted to quick successive strikes and acrobatic lunges. The master can turn one opening into a strike for two and has learned to deflect even powerful blows with a simple wooden stick.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Double Ended |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Double Ended, Lunge |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Double Ended, Lunge, Trip |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Deflect, Double Ended, Lunge, Trip |
| Master Ability | If you have the Extra Attack feature, you may make two attacks instead of one when you use this weapon's Double Ended property or when you make an opportunity attack. |

\column

#### Flanged Mace

A metal head with bladed protrusions, attached to a simple shaft designed specifically to hammer and shred armor. Masters punch through any armor to damage foes with ease.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Penetrate |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Master Ability | Your penetrate ignores 3/4 of enemies armor bonus to their Armor Class, instead of 1/2 |

#### Great Club

A simple, heavy, two-handed club, though it can be refined like the Japanese Tetsubo. A master of the greatclub can render a weapon nearly useless by smashing it bent or broken.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Knockback |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Knockback, Penetrate |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Disarm, Heavy, Knockback, Penetrate |
| Master Ability | If you score a critical hit, your enemy must succeed on a Reflex check, or their mundane weapon suffers a permanent disadvantage on attack rolls until it is
repaired. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Bludgeons }}

\page

#### Heavy Club

A larger mass weapon, much like a bat or ball mace. A master can target the foe's head more easily, disorienting and disabling their foes with a wound-up swing for the fences.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Versatile |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Thrown (10/40), Versatile |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Thrown (20/60), Versatile |
| Master Ability | If you score a critical hit, your enemy must succeed on a Constitution check or suffer disadvantage to all attacks and ability checks until the end of its next turn. |

#### Light Club

A simple sap or a metal bar, many clubs used for combat are designed to be thrown. Some light clubs are designed for policing, intended to be less-than-lethal, while others can be shorn in spikes or sharpened rings with a broad spiked tip. A master is extremely accurate at a foe's head to knock them off balance.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Thrown (40/80) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Thrown (40/80) |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit, your foe must succeed on a Constitution check or suffer disadvantage to its Fortitude and Wisdom based ability checks until the end of your next turn. |

#### Mallet

Typically a crafter's tool, consisting of a shallow cylinder on a short handle. The lighter, faster bludgeon takes unique opportunities that other bludgeons would miss. A master uses the lightness of a mallet for a quick strike that sends the enemy reeling.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Master Ability | If you choose the attack action, as a bonus action, you can make a shove attempt which, if successful, deals this weapon's damage. |

\column

#### Morningstar

An infantry weapon in the form of a thick wooden shaft up to 8 feet in length, slightly fluted toward the top, with a spiked head and topped with a stout iron spike. This reach weapon gives infantry an advantage against armored opponents without needing to learn advanced techniques, enabling simple militias to protect themselves from armor. A master with a morning star can absolutely ruin armor, rendering it less effective for its wearer.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Penetrate |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Penetrate, Reach |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Brace, Penetrate, Reach |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Brace, Double Ended, Penetrate, Reach |
| Master Ability | If you score a critical hit, your target's armor bonus to their AC is reduced by 1. This effect can stack until the target has no armor bonus to their AC, and is not removed until the armor has been repaired |

#### Quarterstaff

A quarterstaff is a heavier, thicker staff, meant for more weight and power in blocking than quick strikes in succession. Sometimes shod in iron, this staff provides increased protection for the master, able to use its shodding and length to provide a more stable means of defense.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Double Ended |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Double Ended, Reach |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Double Ended, Reach, Trip |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Double Ended, Reach, Trip |
| Master Ability | You gain +1 weapon AC. Additionally, when you attack a foe that is more than 5ft away from you, your weapon damage becomes d10 |

{{pageNumber,auto}}

{{wide
### Bows and Slings
| Weapon | Damage Types | Untrained Damage | Trained Damage | Experience Damage | Expert Damage | Master Damage | Weight | Cost |
|:-------|:------------:|:----------------:|:--------------:|:-----------------:|:-------------:|:-------------:|:------:|:----:|
| Bladed Bow | Piercing or Slashing | d8 | d6, d8 | d6, d8 | d6, d8 | d6 [d6], d8 | 5 | 100 |

| Greatbow | Piercing | d10 | d10 | d10 | d10 | d12 | 5 | 75 |
| Longbow | Piercing | d8 | d8 | d8 | d8 | d10 | 2 | 50 |
| Recurve | Piercing | d8 | d8 | d8 | d8 | 2d4 | 2 | 75 |

#### Bladed Bow

Two curved blades affixed to longbow length limbs. Though not nearly as stout as a quarterstaff due to the flexibility of the bow itself, it is nonetheless an effective way to fight the close enemy. The bladed bow is very specialized and requires dedicated training to be anything but clumsy but in the hands of a master, the blade bow can protect a retreat as easily as it can press a melee attack.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (100/500), Awkward, Reload Reaction, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (60/150), Melee d6, Reload Free, Heavy |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (60/150), Melee d6, Reload Free, Heavy |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (120/600), Melee d6, Reload Free, Heavy |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (120/600), Melee d6, Reload Free, Double Ended, Heavy |
| Master Ability | While holding this weapon, your movement does not incur opportunity attacks. |

\column

#### Compound

About the size of a shortbow, but has two pulleys on the limbs which allow the user to load exponentially more force. Because of the added mechanical aspect, loading is a bit slower than loading other bows, but its stopping power punches like a crossbow. A master can overdraw the pulleys to punch through targets like a crossbow.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (100/500), Awkward, Reload Reaction |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (100/500), Reload Free |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (200/800), Reload Free |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (200/800), Reload Free, Puncture |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (200/800), Reload Free, Puncture |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit, you deal normal damage to your primary target and weapon damage to one other target in a straight line from you that intersects your first target, as long as your attack roll would hit your second target's AC as well. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Bows and Slings }}

\page

#### Greatbow

Much taller and stouter than the longbow, easily reaching 6ft-8ft in length and as thick as a quarterstaff. It launches specialized great arrows that are similar in size to a javelin. Due to its size, javelins and ballista bolts can be used as ammunition, but with disadvantage to the attack roll. Greatbow masters can overdraw the stout poundage, sending enemies flying back. You must have a Strength score of at least 13 to wield a Greatbow.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (100/500), Awkward, Reload Reaction, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (100/500), Reload Free, Heavy, Trip |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (100/500), Reload Free, Heavy, Penetrate, Trip |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (200/800), Reload Free, Heavy, Penetrate, Trip |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (200/800), Reload Free, Heavy, Knockback, Penetrate, Trip |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit, you also force your target to save against knockback. All creatures that are flying have disadvantage on this save. |

#### Longbow 

A larger bow than the shortbow, consisting of 5ft-6ft limbs, thick sinew cording bowstring, and a longer powerstroke. Perhaps a bit cumbersome in close combat and atop a mount, even so, a master archer steadies their aim in any situation, ignoring distractions which may impede accuracy.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (100/500), Awkward, Reload Reaction, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (60/150), Reload Free, Heavy |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (120/600), Reload Free, Heavy |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (120/600), Reload Free, Heavy |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (120/600), Reload Free, Heavy |
| Master Ability | If you suffer disadvantage for any reason, you can use your ability action to negate your disadvantage until the end of your turn. You no longer suffer disadvantage to attacks made beyond normal range. |

\column

#### Recurve 

Usually shorter, in the 3ft-4ft range, but with a longer power stroke than a shortbow of its size. Each limb curves away from the wielder at its ends, effectively loading twice the elastic power into the arrow. Due to the shorter overall size but higher draw, the master can load an extra arrow into the recurve and attack two different targets.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (80/320), Awkward, Reload Reaction |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (80/320), Reload Free |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (100/400), Reload Free |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (100/400), Reload Free |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (100/400), Reload Free |
| Master Ability | You can loose two arrows at once with the same power. Once on each of your turns when you make a recurve attack, you can make another recurve attack against a different creature that is within 5 feet of the original target and within normal range. |

#### Shortbow

A simple bow about 3ft in length, more suited to close combat, as its smaller size lends itself to agile movement and quick targeting on either side of the body. Masters with the shortbow can make snap shots as quickly as any swordsman reacts to an opening.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (60/240), Awkward, Reload Reaction |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (60/150), Reload Free |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (80/320), Reload Free, Hipshot |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (80/320), Reload Free, Balanced, Hipshot |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (80/320), Reload Free, Balanced, Hipshot |
| Master Ability | You may use your ability action to make a ranged attack even if you used your action for something else. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Bows and Slings }}

\page

#### Sling

A simple leather cup swung about the body to release a stone with circular momentum. You can launch anything that can fit in the cup; bombs, potions, poisons, even rounded stones, but do so with -1 to the attack. You may also put something into the sling and make a melee attack with it, swinging the weapon like a flail. A master maximizes their power in the throw, and can disable and disorient an enemy with precise shots to the head.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Ranged (30/120), Awkward, Reload Reaction, Conceal, Light |
| Trained    | One Handed, Ranged (30/120), Reload Free, Conceal, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Ranged (60/180), Reload Free, Conceal, Disarm, Light |
| Expert     | One Handed, Ranged (60/180), Reload Free, Conceal, Disarm, Light, Trip |
| Master     | One Handed, Ranged (60/180), Reload Free, Conceal, Disarm, Entangle, Light, Trip |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit, the target must succeed on a Constitution check or suffer disadvantage to attacks until the end of its next turn. |

#### Wrist Shot

Instead of gathering circular momentum, this slingshot uses elastic material to launch anything a sling can without the penalty. A wrist shot is a favorite of smaller folk, more easily able to conceal the weapon and able to make use of ranged attacks with smaller arms and generally weaker stature. Masters with wrist shots can target weak points and make it easier for their allies to land critical blows.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (40/160), Awkward, Reload Reaction, Conceal |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (40/160), Reload Free, Conceal |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (40/160), Reload Free, Conceal, Hipshot |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (40/160), Reload Free, Conceal, Disarm, Hipshot |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (40/160), Reload Free, Conceal, Disarm, Hipshot |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit, your enemy loses its reaction until the start of its next turn. |

#### Broadsword

True broadswords have a wider blade to add power to the cut, and often perform more like an axe in the strike. Examples include the messer, cleaver sword, or Chinese dadao. A master strikes through soft targets, driving their momentum to other targets.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Penetrate |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Keen, Penetrate |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Keen, Penetrate |
| Master Ability | When you score a critical hit or reduce a target to 0 hit points, you can make another attack to another target within 5ft, as part of the same action. This effect can happen multiple times as long as the criteria are met. |

#### Falchion

Descended from the broadsword, the cusped tip and straight blade was a later period design but iconic in appearance, and this two handed version represents the pinnacle of its design. A master maximizes the falchion's cutting power, striking soft targets with critical accuracy.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Disarm |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Disarm, Penetrate |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Keen, Penetrate |
| Master Ability | If your attack is at least 5 higher than your target's AC, your attack is automatically a critical hit |

\column

#### Greatsword

Often as tall as its wielder, spanning in the 5ft-6ft range with a 2ft handle and a lengthy, wide blade. The long blade, lengthy handle, and added weight make the greatsword one of the most damaging melee weapons in use, and can easily dispatch larger targets with ease. A master finds the greatest weapon to use against a large enemy is the greatsword.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Keen |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Keen, Knockback |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Keen, Knockback |
| Master Ability | Against category size Large and larger targets, your damage is 2d12, instead of 2d10. |

#### Katana

A single edged blade, slightly curved with a minimal guard and a long handle. The longer handle and curved edge provide greater leverage for more effective deflections. A master deflects even powerful blows with ease.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Versatile |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Light, Versatile |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Keen, Light, Versatile |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Keen, Light, Versatile |
| Master Ability | While wielding a katana with one hand, you may add your weapon ability modifier to deflect rolls. While wielding with two hands, your deflect dice becomes 2d10. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Combat Blades }}

\page

#### Longsword

A multipurpose sword with a wide guard for dueling, heavy pommel for balance, and a fine, rapier point. Generally a hand and a half handle, this sword is favored by spellblades for its ease of use in one hand or two. Masters become devastatingly accurate, standing up to even master duelists.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Versatile |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Balanced, Versatile |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Balanced, Disarm, Versatile |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Balanced, Disarm, Lunge, Versatile |
| Master Ability | Your critical hit range is 19-20 and while wielding with two hands your critical hit range is 18-20. |

#### Montante

A long greatsword made famous by western Europeans, similar to a polearm in reach and technique thanks to a handle above the guard called a ricasso. The master has learned the famous protection technique, keeping an ally safe with expert application of refined angles and parries.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Reach |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Balanced, Heavy, Reach |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Balanced, Heavy, Reach |
| Master Ability | On your turn, you can use your reaction to enter a protective stance. Until the start of your next turn, all attacks against allies within your reach suffer disadvantage. |

#### Odachi

The famous horse killer blade from late period Japan, the odachi is the greatsword of the east. Its curved cutting edge and huge handle give the master a perfect balance of defense and offense missing from western styles.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Keen, Heavy |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Deflect, Keen, Heavy |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Deflect, Keen, Heavy |
| Master Ability | You deal one additional damage die to your target if you attack a different target than your previous attack. |

\column

#### Scimitar

A single-handed curved sword, with generally more weight in the blade than the pommel. The added agility and pommel weight give the master a sweeping, mobile fighting style that benefits from flowing movement over rigid stance.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Light |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Keen, Light |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Deflect, Keen, Light |
| Master Ability | If you travel at least 20ft or are mounted, your next attack deals an additional d8 damage. |

#### Short Glaive

A glaive weapon with a shorter handle, usually in the range of length of a greatsword, but much lighter as the metal blade is smaller and more than half of the weapon is wooden haft. A short glaive is favored among elven armies as an effective long weapon that is both heavy hitting and light enough to use with finesse. Masters are lightning fast, quickly taking advantage of a miss to make an offensive opening.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Brace |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Brace, Lunge |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Balanced, Brace, Lunge |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Balanced, Brace, Lunge |
| Master Ability | If an enemy you can see misses you with a melee attack, you can use your reaction to make an attack with advantage against that enemy. |

#### War Sword

Child of the Longsword and Greatsword, this sword's length lies between the two, combining both styles. A master deals greater damage against larger targets like the Greatsword, with deft precision of the tip much like a Longsword.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Heavy |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Melee, Heavy, Versatile |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Heavy, Versatile |
| Master Ability | Your critical hit range is 19-20 while wielding with two hands, unless it is already larger. Against category size Large and larger enemies, your damage is 2d8(2d10) instead of d12(2d8). |{{pageNumber,auto}}

#### Blowgun

A tube used to launch a needle dart with your breath. The dart is small and silent, and if you make an attack from stealth and miss, your location is not revealed. A master uses the art of the flying viper, shooting two darts at once and reloading with a single hand.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Free, Awkward, Conceal |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Free, Conceal, Light |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Free, Conceal, Hipshot, Light |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Free, Conceal, Hipshot, Keen, Light |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Free, Conceal, Hipshot, Keen, Light |
| Master Ability | You can load two darts and shoot two with the same attack roll at the same target or to two targets that are within 5 feet of one another. Each dart can deliver a poison or other payload, and this weapon's Keen property applies to any poison it delivers. Apply your weapon ability modifier to only one dart for damage. |

\column

#### Hand Crossbow

A hand drawn bow on a pistol grip, these prods are weaker than other crossbows, but the drawstring can be pulled back without mechanical assistance. A master reloads one-handed, using the bolt case to draw and load in one motion.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Ranged (20/60), Reload Reaction, Awkward, Light |
| Trained    | One Handed, Ranged (30/120), Reload Free, Light |
| Experience | One Handed, Ranged (30/120), Reload Free, Keen, Light |
| Expert     | One Handed, Ranged (30/120), Reload Free, Hipshot, Keen, Light |
| Master     | One Handed, Ranged (60/120), Reload Free, Hipshot, Keen, Light |
| Master Ability | Can be reloaded with one hand. As an ability action, you can make an off-hand attack if you haven't used it for an attack or held your action for an attack. |

#### Heavy Crossbow

A large crossbow with steel prods, loading over a thousand pounds of force. A master arbalist has become deadly accurate with their bolt, maximizing their sniper potential.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (50/200), Reload Attack, Awkward, Heavy, Penetrate |

| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (200/400), Reload Reaction, Heavy, Keen, Penetrate, Puncture, Trip  |
| Master Ability | Every 5 more you roll over your target's AC, you add another weapon damage die. These additional dice are unaffected by a critical hit. |

#### Hidden Crossbow

This wrist-mount is similar to a hidden blade, deploying in secret with one hand. The small mechanism can be pulled back by hooking it onto the needle case to reload one-handed. The master can shoot in melee at the slightest distraction.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Ranged (10/30), Reload Reaction, Affixed, Awkward, Conceal, Light |

| Master Ability | If an enemy misses you with an attack, you can use your reaction to make a ranged attack against it. |

#### Light Crossbow

A simple wooden crossbow drawn by pulling a lever. A master can move and shoot reflexively at moving targets.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (40/200), Reload Ability, Awkward |

#### Mauler

Two bows mounted in an X shape to a tiller which holds three bolts. Even with four prods, the bolts fly with less power than a hand crossbow and don’t group well at distance, but have incredible stopping power up close. Masters group the bolts at weak points with devastating effect.
:
Because the bolts spread over distance, the damage is only 1d4+1 on medium or smaller size targets outside normal range, as only the top bolt is on target. All three bolts hit Large and larger creatures at any range.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Attacl, Awkward |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Ability, Puncture |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Ability, Hipshot, Puncture |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Ability, Hipshot, Keen, Puncture |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (25/100), Reload Reaction, Keen, Hipshot,Puncture |
| Master Ability | If you roll another die with the Puncture property, roll 2d4 instead of 1d4. |

#### Portable Ballista

This small siege weapon is slow to reload with an enormous crannequin but the punch is worth the wait. Masters use flanking surfaces to pin a target with the launched javelin.
:
A deployable stand can be purchased for 150g. As an action, you mount the ballista to the stand. While mounted, its reload is an object interaction, but you cannot move it until you use another action to unmount it.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (150/400), Reload Action, Awkward, Heavy, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (150/600), Reload Attack, Entangle, Heavy, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (150/600), Reload Attack, Entangle, Heavy, Keen, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (150/600), Reload Attack, Entangle, Heavy, Keen, Knockback, Penetrate, Puncture, Trip |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (300/600), Reload Ability, Entangle, Heavy, Keen, Knockback Penetrate, Puncture, Trip |
| Master Ability | Your Entangle attacks add the restrained condition if successful, as you pin your target to surrounding terrain features. |

{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Crossbows }}

\page

#### Repeating Crossbow

Repeaters have a weaker draw strength to allow the user to draw with one hand by pulling a lever along the bottom much like a modern shotgun. It holds 6 bolts and once depleted, you must spend an action to refill the magazine. The master has learned to shoot as they pull the reload lever, dumping shots into a target with speed.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (40/200), Reload Free, Awkward |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (80/320), Reload Free |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (80/320), Reload Free, Keen |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (80/320), Reload Free, Keen |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (160/320), Reload Free, Keen |
| Master Ability | You may use your ability action as an attack action if you do not move on your turn. |

#### Spinner

This gnomish invention launches discus blades with internal mechanisms instead of prods. It holds ten blades, reloading for free by pulling the level located at the back of the weapon. When depleted, you must spend an action to reload ten more. Masters can attack several targets at once by expertly planning their ricochet path.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Ranged (20/60), Reload Free, Awkward |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Ranged (30/120), Reload Free |
| Experience | Two Handed, Ranged (30/120), Reload Free, Hipshot |
| Expert     | Two Handed, Ranged (30/120), Reload Free, Disarm, Hipshot |
| Master     | Two Handed, Ranged (60/120), Reload Free, Disarm, Hipshot |
| Master Ability | As an action, you can choose up to 5 distinct targets, within 10ft of your first target to all be the target of a single attack roll. Roll damage separately for each target you hit. |
