#### Bolas

A pair of weights connected to a reinforced cord or chain to bind a target's limbs. The master bolo accurately targets the legs to bind and trip in one attack.
:
A normal bolas has an 15AC, 2HP and is immune to bludgeoning damage, but more sturdy versions may exist. When your enemy escapes from or reduces the bolas to 0hp, it is destroyed.
:
Bolas are a type of weapon that uses the Entangle property even if no one is holding the weapon.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Thrown (10/30) |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Thrown (20/30) |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Entangle, Thrown (40/60) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Entangle, Thrown (40/60), Trip |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Entangle, Thrown (40/60), Trip |
| Master Ability | When your entangle attack hits, the target must succeed on the save or become prone and restrained. |

#### Boomerang

A hooked wing, sharpened on the inner curve and used like a cudgel. The master can curve its flight path to hit more than one target with a powerful throw.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light, Thrown (30/120) |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (40/120) |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Light, Thrown (40/120) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Light, Thrown (80/240) |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Light, Thrown (80/240) |
| Master Ability | Once on your turn, you can choose two targets within 40ft to attack with the same attack. |

\column

#### Chakram

A sharpened discus or ring, sturdy enough to be used in melee. Dangerous from all angles, the master uses any opening as an opportunity for a quick throw or slash.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (40/120) |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Keen, Light, Thrown (40/120) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Keen, Light, Thrown (80/500) |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Keen, Light, Thrown (80/500) |
| Master Ability | If a creature misses you with an attack, as a reaction you can attack that creature. |

#### Dart

A short rod fletched like an arrow with a weighted tip. A master pins targets with precision aimed at clothing.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (30/60) |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Light, Penetrate, Thrown (30/60) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Light, Penetrate, Puncture, Thrown (60/120) |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Light, Penetrate, Puncture, Thrown (60/120) |
| Master Ability | You can choose to deal no damage on hit and pin the enemy to an adjacent wall or obstacle causing your enemy to be restrained. The escape DC is your weapon DC. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Throwing Weapons }}

\page

#### Kunai

A small, dagger-like tool of Japanese origin derived from a masonry trowel. Its ring pommel and wide design allow for unique utility with rope, and in the hands of a master, the heavier design allows for deflections mid-flight.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Deflect, Light, Thrown (30/90) |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Deflect, Light, Thrown (30/90) |
| Master Ability | You can use your deflect property within your normal thrown range, and for any creature of your choice. |

#### Net

A Large or smaller creature hit by a net is restrained until freed. It has no effect on creatures that are formless or Huge or larger. Dealing 5 slashing damage to the net (AC10) ends the restrained condition and destroys the net. Masters can toss the net in a way that tangles it around their prey, making it much harder to escape.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | Two Handed, Melee, Awkward, Entangle, Thrown (5/10) |
| Trained    | Two Handed, Melee, Entangle, Thrown (10/20) |
| Experience | Two Handed, Melee, Entangle, Thrown (10/20), Trip |
| Master     | Two Handed, Melee, Entangle, Light, Thrown (15/30), Trip |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Entangle, Light, Thrown (15/30), Trip |
| Master Ability | 	The net's AC is increased by 10. If you have advantage on an entangle attack, your target has disadvantage on the check made to escape. |

\column

#### Throwing Knife

Small, balanced knives with a broad piercing tip and sharpened pommel, no longer than 4"-6". Easily hidden, these blades offer more range than throwing stars due to the higher weighted pommel. A master has perfected the art of quick throws at their enemy's hands or arms as they swing a weapon, causing the knife to interfere with their attack.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Light, Thrown (30/90) |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Thrown (30/90) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Thrown (60/120) |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Thrown (60/120) |
| Master Ability | You can choose to deal only your weapon ability modifier in damage, but force your target to succeed on a Reflex check or lose its reaction and suffer disadvantage on its next attack roll. |

#### Throwing Shot

Though not strictly their invention, the technique to throw an iron ball in combat was pioneered by the Orcs. Not many can stand up to the heavy iron in flight. A master is deadly accurate with the shot and is able to target an enemy's head to stun if they have an advantage. A creature with Strength less than 13 cannot wield a shot at all.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Thrown (10/10) |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Penetrate, Thrown (20/60) |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Knockback, Penetrate, Thrown (20/60) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Knockback, Penetrate, Thrown (30/90), Trip |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Disarm, Knockback, Penetrate, Thrown (30/90), Trip, Versatile |
| Master Ability | If you have advantage and both dice would have hit, or if you score a critical hit, your enemy must succeed on a Constitution check or be stunned until the end of its next turn. If you have disadvantage but one dice would have hit, deal your weapon ability modifier in damage, though this still counts as a miss. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Throwing Weapons }}

\page

#### Throwing Star

Star shaped metal disks made to be palmed together and thrown as a pepper of smaller strikes to disable an enemy before a followup attack. The flat, small design of these weapons allows many to be palmed at once and thrown all together. A master has the capability to dance in a quick circle, throwing stars at all foes around them.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Untrained  | One Handed, Melee, Awkward, Light, Thrown (10/30) |
| Trained    | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Thrown (20/60) |
| Experience | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Nimble, Thrown (20/60) |
| Master     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Nimble, Thrown (40/120) |
| Expert     | One Handed, Melee, Conceal, Light, Nimble, Thrown (40/120) |
| Master Ability | As an action, you can make a single attack against all targets of your choice within 20 ft of you. You must have enough throwing stars to attack each target. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Throwing Weapons }}

\page

{{wide
### Natural Weapons
| Weapon | Damage Types | Damage |
|:-------|:------------:|:------:|
| All | [None] | All natural weapons weapon die increase by 1 dice size at experienced (for example, from 1d4 to 1d6), and increase by one more size at master (for example, from 1d6 to 1d8). The starting damage is determined by the weapon ability description |
| Bite | Piercing | [See above] |
| Claw | Slashing | [See above] |
| Horns | Piercing | [See above] |
| Slam | Bludgeoning | [See above] |
| Tail | Bludgeoning | [See above] |
| Wings | Slashing | [See above] |
}}
:
A creature with a natural weapon will always have at least a +2 (Trained) ability modifier with their natural weapon, so the Untrained properties will not be listed. For all Natural weapons except Claws, no hands are needed to use them

#### Bite

If a creature is two size categories bigger than the creature it is biting, the bite grapples on hit. This listing can be used for any other attack which originates from the mouth, e.g mandibles, beaks, maw, etc

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Trained    | Natural, Melee, Puncture |
| Experience | Natural, Melee, Nimble, Puncture |
| Master     | Natural, Melee, Entangle, Nimble, Puncture |
| Expert     | Natural, Melee, Barbed, Entangle, Nimble, Puncture |
| Master Ability | When you successfully entangle your target you also deal your full weapon damage. While your enemy is entangled, it suffers disadvantage to checks made to escape your grapple |

#### Claw

Claws adorn the hands of most predators and can be used in the takedown and grapple of prey. Claw asters use their grappling as offensive tools in this egard. This listing can be used for any other natural weapons which are at the end of an appendage, e.g. pincers, talons, impale, etc. If your claws are retractable, you gain the Conceal property.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Trained    | Natural, One-Handed, Melee, Affixed, Light |
| Experience | Natural, One-Handed, Melee, Affixed, Entangle, Light |
| Master     | Natural, One-Handed, Melee, Affixed, Entangle, Light, Nimble |
| Expert     | Natural, One-Handed, Melee, Affixed, Entangle, Keen, Light, Nimble |
| Master Ability | 	If you succeed in a grapple contest to impose or escape the grappled condition, you deal your weapon's damage to your target. |

\column

#### Horns

Horns are among the strongest organic materials and can easily punch through tough hide and thick armor. This listing can be used for any attack which is of a similar source, e.g. spike, gore, ram, etc.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Trained    | Natural, Melee, Penetrate |
| Experience | Natural, Melee, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Master     | Natural, Melee, Brace, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Expert     | Natural, Melee, Brace, Deflect, Penetrate, Puncture |
| Master Ability | When you move at least 20 feet, you can make one melee attack with your horns as an ability action. If this attack hits, it counts as a critical hit. |

#### Slam

Creatures with bulk or lacking in obvious teeth and claws can use their weight against a target. A creature two size categories larger than its target always applies the stagger property to each attack. This listing can be used for any other blunt attack, e.g. hooves, fist, stomp, etc.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Trained    | Natural, Melee, Heavy |
| Experience | Natural, Melee, Brace, Heavy |
| Master     | Natural, Melee, Brace, Heavy, Knockback |
| Expert     | Natural, Melee, Brace, Heavy, Knockback |
| Master Ability | If you move at least 20ft straight toward an enemy and land a slam attack in the same turn, that enemy must succeed on an Athletics check or be knocked prone and you can make an additional slam attack as an ability action. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Natural Weapons }}

\page

#### Tail

Most tails are not prehensile, but a tail can be used for a surprise swipe either at an enemy's feet or an off angle at their sword hand, possibly disarming them. This listing can be used for any other long, tail-like attack, e.g. pseudopod, tentacle, tendril, etc.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Trained    | Natural, Melee, Trip |
| Experience | Natural, Melee, Knockback, Trip |
| Master     | Natural, Melee, Entangle, Knockback, Trip |
| Expert     | Natural, Melee, Disarm, Entangle, Knockback, Trip |
| Master Ability | When you hit with a normal attack, your target must succeed on a Reflex check or be knocked prone. |

#### Wings

While most wings are too delicate to be used as a weapon, they can be used in an emergency for defensive purposes. If your wings have no damage listing, they use deflect d6, otherwise using the damage listed for the attack.

| | |
|:-----------|:------|
| Trained    | Natural, Melee, Knockback |
| Experience | Natural, Melee, Deflect, Knockback |
| Master     | Natural, Melee, Deflect, Knockback, Trip |
| Expert     | Natural, Melee, Deflect, Knockback, Lunge, Trip |
| Master Ability | As an action, you can flap your wings and create a powerful gust of wind. All creatures in a 15ft cone in front of you must succeed on an Athletics or Reflex Saving Throw or be your choice of pushed back 5ft or prone. |

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Natural Weapons }}

\page

## Armor

This section describes the basic armors available in Natural Progressions. Armors directly affect your character's Armor Class, and generally is the second biggest modifier behind your reflex skill modifier. As stated above, your Armor Class is calculated as follows:
:
10 + armor bonus + weapon bonus + shield bonus + reflex skill modifier
:
Unlike weapons and skills, armors do not have a skill modifier that increase with a natural 20. The reflex skill modifier fulfills this role for the Armor Class calculation.
:
However, like weapons, there are different types of armors: light armor, medium armor, and heavy armor. In order to use any of these types of armor, you need to be trained in them - a character is either trained or untrained in each type of armor. This training status is gotten by your Race/Culture, Background and Class.
:
Additionally, your type of armor can affect your stealth skill - some armors give disadvantage to stealth checks while being worn.

{{wide
### Light Armor
| Type | AC Bonus | Stealth | Weight | Gold Cost |
|:-----|:--------:|:-------:|:------:|:---------:|
| Padded | 1 | Disadvantage | 4 | 5 |
| Leather | 1 | None | 5 | 10 |
| Studded | 2 | None | 6 | 45 |
| Lacquered | 3 | Disadvantage | 6 | 300 |
}}

#### Padded
Thick padding made of quilted fabrics or furs, this armor provides little more than slight protection from incidental contact, and restricts the wearer's movement.

#### Leather
Moderately thin, unhardened utility leather that offers slight protection but is cheap and flexible.

\column

#### Studded Leather
Thick, hard leather hide that has been studded with metal rivets or scales. The increased time and material to stud the leather adds to the manufacturing cost.

#### Lacquered Leather
This leather has been boiled in wax or water and painted with lacquer to toughen it as hard as modern plastics. It offers superior protection to other light armors, but the required skill to create it greatly adds to the cost. Additionally, the hard plates create more noise than softer armors, leaving much to be desired by stealthy assassins.

{{wide
### Medium Armor
| Type | AC Bonus | Stealth | Weight | Gold Cost |
|:-----|:--------:|:-------:|:------:|:---------:|
| Chain Shirt | 3 | Disadvantage | 10 | 50 |
| Ring Mail | 4 | None | 12 | 100 |
| Breastplate | 5 | None | 10 | 300 |
| Banded Mail | 6 | Disadvantage | 20 | 500 |
}}

#### Chain Shirt
This simple shirt of butted mail is easy to produce as the rings aren't welded closed. A chain shirt covers less than a hauberk but is lighter and more affordable.

#### Ring Mail
A pattern of closed rings stitched to a thick leather backing. This armor takes about as long as a Chain shirt to make and is similar in cost, but due to the combined protection of the leather backing and metal rings, offers greater protection than either one separately. Unfortunately, this combined armor is more restrictive.

\column

#### Breastplate
Wearing just the breastplate of a suit of plate armor, this armor provides the easiest mobility of the medium armors and more protection than the chain shirt or ring mail. However, plate is expensive to make and thus has a greatly increased cost.

#### Banded Mail
The quintessential half-plate, also known as lorica, this armor is a series of metal ribbons banded together to form more complete protection. Banded mail is cheaper to produce than full plate, but is still quite a process, involving many steel plates and precise shaping.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Armor }}

\page

{{wide
### Heavy Armor
| Type | AC Bonus | Stealth | Weight | Gold Cost |
|:-----|:--------:|:-------:|:------:|:---------:|
| Hauberk | 5 | Disadvantage |25 | 150 |
| Scale Mail | 6 | Disadvantage | 30 | 300 |
| Split | 7 | Disadvantage | 33 | 750 |
| Plate | 8 | Disadvantage | 40 | 1500 |
}}

#### Hauberk
A full coat of chainmail made with durable, riveted or welded rings in a tight weave. The Hauberk covers both arms and stops at the knee, offering near complete coverage.

#### Scale
Adding a scale to each ring in a hauberk gives a substantial increase to protection without much increase in the manufacturing but adds quite a bit of weight.

#### Splint
Splint armor can be described as the poor man’s plate. Instead of plates shaped to fit, a series of small, palm-sized plates and finger sized “splints” of metal are tied together to form a coat. It is cheaper to produce but is not as durable.

#### Plate
Plate is extremely difficult and costly to produce, however, no other armor is more protective. All parts of the body are covered, even the wearer's joints.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Armor }}

\page

## Shields

Like armor, shields are a part of the Armor Class calculation and do not have an ability modifier associated with them - characters are trained or untrained with Shields.
:
Unlike armor, characters still get the AC Bonus associated with each shield if they are untrained.
:
For every shield, there is a time to don, and that can be different depending if the shield is held or strapped. Shields that are strapped cannot be disarmed, however, a strapped shield is considered using the shield with one hand. This does mean that in order to perform an activity, such as wielding a Great Sword, you would need to doff any shield you are using.

{{wide
| Shield | AC Bonus | Stealth | Don (strapped) | Don (Held) | Weight | Cost |
|:-------|:--------:|:-------:|:--------------:|:----------:|:------:|:----:|
| Arm Guard | 1 | Normal | N/A | Free | 1 | 10 |
| Buckler | 1 | Normal | N/A | Free | 3 | 5 |
| Diskarmor | 2 | Normal | N/A | Ability Action | 5 | 150 |
| Kite | 3 | Disadvantage | Action | Action | 10 | 50 |
| Pavise | 1 (3) | Disadvantage | N/A | N/A | 15  | 35 |
| Skirmish | 2 | Normal | Action | Ability Action | 6 | 10 |
| Spiked | 2 | Disadvantage | Action | Ability Action | 8 | 20 |
| Tower | 3 | Disadvantage | Action | Action | 20 | 50 |
}}

#### Arm Guard
A fully enclosed arm shield that often had a sword built into is construction to make a gauntlet sword called a pata. Without an attached weapon, the hand which has an arm guard equipped can be used to help wield a weapon or assist with Reload, but cannot be used to wield a weapon by itself; in this case it must be attached to the arm guard. The master has perfected this fighting style.
:
When trained with Arm Guards, you may attach a light weapon to an arm guard as part of a rest using smith's tools. The weapon gains the affixed property but can't be removed without smith's tools.

#### Buckler

A buckler, or target, is a hand shield used by duelists and fencers for its small profile and ease of counter attacks while deflecting. The master's trained duelist techniques set them up for the perfect riposte.
:
When trained with Bucklers, bucklers gain the Deflect (d8) weapon trait.

#### Diskarmor

An esoteric weapon of gnomish invention, a diskarmor is a round shield attached to a chain mechanism that retracts quickly after the chain reaches its length to make essentially a shield yo-yo. The user can toss it out to wield it like a large flail, then retract it to be used as a shield again.
:
When trained with Diskarmors, the shield games the following properties: One Handed, Melee d6, Entangle, Reach, Trip. Diskarmor deals bludgeoning damage. A diskarmor is not considered a weapon.

#### Kite

Kite shields are as wide as the wielder's torso but extend downward with a point or oval extension to protect the legs, which can also be used offensively to knock an enemy off guard.
:
When trained with Kite sheilds, you gain advantage on any ability check made to resist being knocked prone or moved along the ground.

#### Pavise

A pavise is a lighter tower shield with a central spike to drive into the ground, or a set of legs to allow the shield to stand freely. While deployed, you can use it as cover. Unfortunately it is unwieldable as a normal shield, only able to be worn on the back. While wearing it, you are unable to equip any other shield.
:
While deployed, a Pavise can be knocked down if the enemy succeeds on an Athletics Check against your Weapon DC. As an ability action you can pick up a pavise and either deploy it again or don it on your back.
:
When trained with Pavise shields, as an ability action, you can drive the shield into the ground, essentially creating an obstacle on the battlefield. When in the 5 x 5 square directly behind the embedded shield, you gain +3 to your armor class (rather than +1), and you are considered covered by the shield. The

#### Skirmish

Skirmish shields come in a variety of shapes but are about the size of the user's torso. A Skirmish shield is large enough to provide better passive protection than the buckler, while still providing the agility missing with a tower shield. The master can extend this agility to even spell attacks and can offensively use the edge of their shield.
:
When trained with Skirmish shields, you gain an additional +2 shield AC against ranged weapon and spell attacks.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Shields }}

\page

#### Spiked

A spiked shield is a blanket term for all weaponized shields, with spikes on the face and either a spiked or bladed edge. Somewhat cumbersome compared to a skirmish shield with the added weaponization, a spiked shield is hard to be stealthy and agile with.
:
When trained with spiked shields, the shield has the following properties: One Handed, Melee d6, Brace, Puncture, Thrown (20/60). Spiked shield deals piercing or slashing damage. A spiked shield is not considered a weapon.

#### Tower

This massive shield is as tall as you and just as wide; you more fight around it like a door as a piece of mobile cover. The master shieldman can take cover at a moment's notice, effectively giving the enemy no target.
:
When trained with tower shields and using the shield as cover, if you are subjected to an effect that allows you to make a Reflex check, and you fail that check, you take only half damage.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Shields }}

\page

## Tools

Unlike many other system, most objects in Natural Progressions besides weapons and money are embedded within different tool kits. Each toolkit comes with different objects and usages as described for the kit.
:
Like weapons and skills, each type of toolkit has its own separate equipment  modifier, to a maximum of +11 to your 1d20 roll. This does mean that at higher equipment modifiers, your character may start to auto-pass certain activies with a tool kit. In such situations, at the discretion of your LM, you may not roll for those activities.
:
Each of the tools is structured as follows:

### Name of Tool
Cost, Weight
:
Description of the tools
:
**Components**. What items one could expect to find in the tool kit.
:
**Skills**. Skills listed here have increased effect with usage of the tool. Some of the effects using the skill are definted in the **Other Activities** section. For these effects, when you make your skill check, you roll a d20, add your tool modifier, and compare to the presented Difficulty Class.
:
For activities not listed in **Other Activities**, when you make your skill check, you roll a d20, add your skill modifier and half of your tool modifier. In either case, if you roll a natural 20, both the skill and tool modifier increases by 1.
:
**Specific Activity**. Some tools have specific activies associated with them. Is activity is unique, and should be referred to when determining effects or rules.
:
**Other Activities**. At the end of each tool is the **Other Activities** table. This lists some standard usages of the tool with their associated Difficulty Class. For these activites, or other actions that use the tool that don't fit into a skill check, roll a d20 and add your tool modifier to the roll.

### Alchemist's Supplies
50 gp, 8 lb
:
Alchemist's supplies enable a character to produce useful concoctions, such as acid or alchemist's fire.
:
**Components**. Alchemist's supplies include two glass beakers, a metal frame to hold a beaker in place over an open flame, a glass stirring rod, a small mortar and pestle, and a pouch of common alchemical ingredients, including salt, powdered iron, and purified water.
:
**Investigation**. When you inspect an area for clues, utilizing Alchemist's supplies allows you to glean additional insight into any chemicals or other substances that might have been used in the area.
:
**Alchemical Crafting**. A character can spend money to collect raw materials, which weigh 1 pound for every 25 gp spent. Each point of raw materials allows you to make one item, and you can only make one item per day.
:
Some items that can be crafted include:
 - **A Vial of Acid**, which can be thrown onto a target. The target must make a Reflex Saving Throw. On a failure, the target takes 2d6 acid damage
 - **Alchemist's Fire**, a fluid that ignites upon contact with the air. A flask of alchemist's fire can be thrown onto a target within 20 ft. The target must make a reflex check. On a failure, the target takes 1d4 fire damage each round, including the round it was hit, until it uses an action and passes the reflex check.
 - **A Vial of Antitoxin**, which allows the consumer to gain advantage on checks against poison for 1 hour.
 - **A Flask of Oil**, which can be used as fuel in a lantern. In combat, this flask can be thrown on the ground as an action, covering 1 square. If lit, it burns for 2 rounds and any character that starts their turn in the square or passes through the square while the oil is list takes 5 fire damage.
 - **A Bottle of Perfume**, which allows adventurers to hide their horrid stink temporarily
 - **A Bar of Soap**, which allows adventurers to remove their stink

**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Create a puff of thick smoke | 10 |
| Identify a poison | 10 |
| Identify a substance | 15 |
| Start a fire | 15 |
| Neutralize an acid | 20 |

### Brewer's Supplies
20 gp, 9 lb
:
Brewing is the art of producing beer. Not only does beer serve as an alcoholic beverage, but the process of brewing purifies water. Crafting beer takes weeks of fermentation, but only a few hours of work.
:
**Components**. Brewer's supplies include a large glass jug, a quantity of hops, a siphon, and several feet of tubing.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Tools }}

\page

**Medicine**. This tool grants additional insight when you treat anyone suffering from alcohol poisoning or when you can use alcohol to dull pain.
:
**Persuasion**. A stiff drink can help soften the hardest heart. Using brewer's supplies can help you ply someone with drink, giving them just enough alcohol to mellow their mood.
:
**Potable Water**. Your knowledge of brewing enables you to purify water that would otherwise be undrinkable. As part of a rest, you can purify up to 6 gallons of water, or 1 gallon as part of a rest.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Detect poison or impurities in a drink | 10 |
| Identify alcohol | 15 |
| Ignore effects of alcohol | 20 |

### Calligrapher's Supplies
10 gp, 5 lb.
:
Calligraphy treats writing as a delicate, beautiful art. Calligraphers produce text that is pleasing to the eye, using a style that is difficult to forge. Their supplies also give them some ability to examine scripts and determine if they are legitimate, since a calligrapher's training involves long hours of studying writing and attempting to replicate its style and design.
:
**Components**. Calligrapher's supplies include ink, a dozen sheets of parchment, and three quills.
:
**Arcana**. Although calligraphy is of little help in deciphering the content of magical writings, these supplies can aid in identifying who wrote a script of a magical nature.
:
**History**. This tool can augment the benefit of successful checks made to analyze or investigate ancient writings, scrolls, or other texts, including runes etched in stone or messages in frescoes or other displays.
:
**Decipher Treasure Map**. This tool grants you expertise in examining maps. You can make an Investigation check to determine a map's age, whether a map includes any hidden messages, or similar facts.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Identify writer of nonmagical script | 10 |
| Determine writer's state of mind | 15 |
| Spot forged text | 15 |
| Forge a signature | 20 |

\column

### Carpenter's Tools
8 gp, 6 lb.
:
Skill at carpentry enables a character to construct wooden structures. A carpenter can build a house, a shack, a wooden cabinet, or similar items.
:
**Components**. Carpenter's tools include a saw, a hammer, nails, a hatchet, a square, a ruler, an adze, a plane, and a chisel.
:
**History**. This tool aids you in identifying the use and the origin of wooden buildings and other large wooden objects.
:
**Investigation**. You gain additional insight when inspecting areas within wooden structures, because you know tricks of construction that can conceal areas from discovery.
:
**Perception**. You can spot irregularities in wooden walls or floors, making it easier to find trap doors and secret passages.
:
**Stealth**. You can quickly assess the weak spots in a wooden floor, making it easier to avoid the places that creak and groan when they're stepped on.
:
**Fortify**. With 1 minute of work and raw materials, you can make a door or window harder to force open. Increase the DC needed to open it by 5.
:
**Temporary Shelter**. As part of a rest, you can construct a lean-to or a similar shelter to keep your group dry and in the shade for the duration of the rest. Because it was fashioned quickly from whatever wood was available, the shelter collapses 1d3 days after being assembled.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Build a simple wooden structure | 10 |
| Design a complex wooden structure | 15 |
| Find a weak point in a wooden wall | 15 |
| Pry apart a door | 20 |

### Cartographer's Tools
15 gp, 6 lb.
:
Using cartographer's tools, you can create accurate maps to make travel easier for yourself and those who come after you. These maps can range from large-scale depictions of mountain ranges to diagrams that show the layout of a dungeon level.
:
**Components**. Cartographer's tools consist of a quill, ink, parchment, a pair of compasses, calipers, and a ruler.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Tools }}

\page

**Arcana, History, Religion**. You can use your knowledge of maps and locations to unearth more detailed information when you use these skills. For instance, you might spot hidden messages in a map, identify when the map was made to determine if geographical features have changed since then, and so forth.
:
**Nature**. Your familiarity with physical geography makes it easier for you to answer questions or solve issues relating to the terrain around you.
:
**Survival**. Your understanding of geography makes it easier to find paths to civilization, to predict areas where villages or towns might be found, and to avoid becoming lost. You have studied so many maps that common patterns, such as how trade routes evolve and where settlements arise in relation to geographic locations, are familiar to you.
:
**Craft a Map**. While traveling, you can draw a map as you go in addition to engaging in other activity.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Determine a map's age and origin | 10 |
| Estimate direction and distance to a landmark | 15 |
| Discern that a map is fake | 15 |
| Fill in a missing part of a map | 20 |

### Climber's Kit
25 gp, 12 lb.
:
A climber's kit is a much needed item for any adventure that wishes to traverse rugged terrain.
:
**Components**. A climber's kit includes special pitons, boot tips, gloves, and a harness.
:
**Investigation**. Your usage of a Climber's Kit gives you unique insight into rappelling down and climbing up a wall. It is easier for you to determine where you should attempt to rappel or climb and to determine if a wall has seen recent activity from those with a Climber's Kit.
:
**Athletics, Performance**. Your skill with a Climber's Kit allows you to attempt public climbing feats more easily. For instance, you could enter a climbing contest and have a leg up on your competition.
:
**Anchor**: As an action, you can use your Climber's Kit to anchor youself. While anchored, you cannot fall or move more than 25 ft from your anchor point. If you are currently falling, you cannot use this action.
:
**Other Activites**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Climb or rappel down a normal wall | 10 |
| Estimate the expected difficulty for climbing an object | 10 |
| Determine the best place to climb | 15 |
| Swing while anchored | 20 |

### Cobbler's Tools
5 gp, 5 lb.
:
Although the cobbler's trade might seem too humble for an adventurer, a good pair of boots will see a character across rugged wilderness and through deadly dungeons.
:
**Components**. Cobbler's tools consist of a hammer, an awl, a knife, a shoe stand, a cutter, spare leather, and thread.
:
**Arcana, History**. Your knowledge of shoes aids you in identifying the magical properties of enchanted boots or the history of such items.
:
**Investigation**. Footwear holds a surprising number of secrets. You can learn where someone has recently visited by examining the wear and the dirt that has accumulated on their shoes. Your experience in repairing shoes makes it easier for you to identify where damage might come from.
:
**Maintain Shoes**. As part of a rest, you can repair your companions' shoes. For the next 24 hours, up to six creatures of your choice who wear shoes you worked on can travel up to 10 hours a day without making saving throws to avoid exhaustion.
:
**Craft Hidden Compartment**. With 8 hours of work, you can add a hidden compartment to a pair of shoes. The compartment can hold an object up to 3 inches long and 1 inch wide and deep. An Investigation or Cobbler's Tool check is needed to discover this compartment if you don't know it exists
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Determine a shoe's age and origin | 10 |
| Find a hidden compartment in a boot heel | 15 |

### Cook's Utensils
1 gp, 8 lb.
:
Adventuring is a hard life. With a cook along on the journey, your meals will be much better than the typical mix of hardtack and dried fruit.
:
**Components**. Cook's utensils include a metal pot, knives, forks, a stirring spoon, and a ladle.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Tools }}

\page

**History**. Your knowledge of cooking techniques allows you to assess the social patterns involved in a culture's eating habits.
:
**Medicine**. When administering treatment, you can transform medicine that is bitter or sour into a pleasing concoction.
:
**Survival**. When foraging for food, you can make do with ingredients you scavenge that others would be unable to transform into nourishing meals.
:
**Prepare Meals**. As part of a rest, you can prepare a tasty meal that helps your companions regain their strength. You and up to five creatures of your choice regain extra hit points equal to your Cook's Utensils modifier, provided you have access to your cook's utensils and sufficient food. This ability does require a successful passing of "Create a typical meal" or "Create a gourmet meal".
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Create a typical meal | 10 |
| Duplicate a meal | 10 |
| Spot poison or impurities in food | 15 |
| Create a gourmet meal | 15 |

### Disguise Kit
25 gp, 3 lb.
:
The perfect tool for anyone who wants to engage in trickery, a disguise kit enables its owner to adopt a false identity.
:
**Components**. A disguise kit includes cosmetics, hair dye, small props, and a few pieces of clothing.
:
**Deception**. In certain cases, a disguise can improve your ability to weave convincing lies.
:
**Intimidation**. The right disguise can make you look more fearsome, whether you want to scare someone away by posing as a plague victim or intimidate a gang of thugs by taking the appearance of a bully.
:
**Performance**. A cunning disguise can enhance an audience's enjoyment of a performance, provided the disguise is properly designed to evoke the desired reaction.
:
**Persuasion**. Folk tend to trust a person in uniform. If you disguise yourself as an authority figure, your efforts to persuade others are often more effective.
:
**Create Disguise**. As part of a rest, you can create a disguise. It takes you 1 minute to don such a disguise once you have created it. You can carry only one such disguise on you at a time without drawing undue attention, unless you have a bag of holding or a similar method to keep them hidden. Each disguise weighs 1 pound.
:
At other times, it takes 10 minutes to craft a disguise that involves moderate changes to your appearance, and 30 minutes for one that requires more extensive changes.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Cover injuries or distinguishing marks | 10 |
| Spot a disguise being used by someone else | 15 |
| Copy a humanoid's appearance | 20 |

### Fisher's Equipment
2 gp, 2 lb.
:
Where there is running water, there generally is fish. For adventurers that spend much of their time in the while, Fisher's Equipment is a must have to provide a steady supply of food.
:
**Components**. Fishing Equipment includes a pole, a line, a hook, and either a lure or some bait.
:
**Insight**. Your knowledge of fishing makes it easier for you to determine if a character is telling the truth when talking about anything related to fishing.
:
**Survival**. As part of a rest, you can attempt to go fishing. For every multiple of 5 you roll, you are able to catch enough fish to feed that amount of people for one day.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Catch fish | 5 |
| Tell if water conditions are good for fishing | 10 |
| Determine if a body of water is polluted or corrupted in a way that would hard the fish| 15 |

### Forgery Kit
15 gp, 5 lb.
:
This small box contains a variety of papers and parchments, pens and inks, seals and sealing wax, gold and silver leaf, and other supplies necessary to create convincing forgeries of physical documents.
:
A forgery kit is designed to duplicate documents and to make it easier to copy a person's seal or signature.
:
**Components**. A forgery kit includes several different types of ink, a variety of parchments and papers, several quills, seals and sealing wax, gold and silver leaf, and small tools to sculpt melted wax to mimic a seal.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Tools }}

\page
**Arcana**. A forgery kit can be used in conjunction with the Arcana skill to determine if a magic item is real or fake.
:
**Deception**. A well-crafted forgery, such as papers proclaiming you to be a noble or a writ that grants you safe passage, can lend credence to a lie.
:
**History**. A forgery kit combined with your knowledge of history improves your ability to create fake historical documents or to tell if an old document is authentic.
:
**Investigation**. When you examine objects, a forgery kit is useful for determining how an object was made and whether it is genuine.
:
**Other Tools**. Knowledge of other tools makes your forgeries that much more believable. For example, you could combine your skill with a forgery kit and your skill with cartographer's tools to make a fake map. When making the forgery check, you would add the average of the two tools being used. Upon a roll of natural 20, both tools would have their modifier increased.
:
**Quick Fake**. As part of a rest, you can produce a forged document no more than one page in length. As part of a rest, you can produce a document that is up to four pages long. Your Intelligence check using a forgery kit determines the DC for someone else's Intelligence (Investigation) check to spot the fake.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Mimic handwriting | 15 |
| Duplicate a wax seal | 20 |

### Glassblower's Tools
30 gp, 5 lb.
:
Someone who is proficient with glassblower's tools has not only the ability to shape glass, but also specialized knowledge of the methods used to produce glass objects.
:
**Components**. The tools include a blowpipe, a small marver, blocks, and tweezers. You need a source of heat to work glass.
:
**Arcana, History**. Your knowledge of glassmaking techniques aids you when you examine glass objects, such as potion bottles or glass items found in a treasure hoard. For instance, you can study how a glass potion bottle has been changed by its contents to help determine a potion's effects. (A potion might leave behind a residue, deform the glass, or stain it.)
:
**Investigation**. When you study an area, your knowledge can aid you if the clues include broken glass or glass objects.
:
**Identify Weakness**. With 1 minute of study, you can identify the weak points in a glass object. Any damage dealt to the object by striking a weak spot is doubled.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Identify source of glass | 10 |
| Determine what a glass object once held | 20 |

### Jeweler's Tools
25 gp, 2 lb.
:
Training with jeweler's tools includes the basic techniques needed to beautify gems. It also gives you expertise in identifying precious stones.
:
**Components**. Jeweler's tools consist of a small saw and hammer, files, pliers, and tweezers.
:
**Arcana**. Jeweler's tools grants you knowledge about the reputed mystical uses of gems. This insight proves handy when you make Arcana checks related to gems or gem-encrusted items.
:
**Investigation**. When you inspect jeweled objects, jeweler's tools aids you in picking out clues they might hold.
:
**Identify Gems**. You can identify gems and determine their value at a glance.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Modify a gem's appearance | 15 |
| Determine a gem's history | 20 |

### Healer's Kit
5 gp, 3 lb.
:
Everyone gets hurt, and every adventurer gets hurt more than the average person.
:
**Components**. This kit is a leather pouch containing enough bandages, salves, and splints for 10 usages of healing.
:
**Medicine**. Your knowledge of healing makes it easier for you to determine the best way to heal a character. 
:
**Stabilize**: As an action, you can stabilize a creature (no roll needed).
:
**Healing**: Once per hour, as an action, you can heal a character. The character heals 2d10 + your Healer's Kit modifier. If the entire hour is spent healing, the character regains 20 + your Healer's Kit modifier.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VI: Equipment | Tools }}

\page
**Other Activities**.
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Stabilize | 1 |
| Healing | 1 |

### Herbalism Kit
5 gp, 3 lb.
:
This kit contains a variety of instruments such as clippers, mortar and pestle, and pouches and vials used by herbalists to create remedies and potions.
:
Using an herbalism kit allows you to identify plants and safely collect their useful elements.
:
**Components**. An herbalism kit includes pouches to store herbs, clippers and leather gloves for collecting plants, a mortar and pestle, and several glass jars.
:
**Arcana**. Your knowledge of the nature and uses of herbs can add insight to your magical studies that deal with plants and your attempts to identify potions.
:
**Investigation**. When you inspect an area overgrown with plants, an herbalism kit can help you pick out details and clues that others might miss.
:
**Medicine**. Your mastery of herbalism improves your ability to treat illnesses and wounds by augmenting your methods of care with medicinal plants. Some plants have the ability to remove specific conditions.
:
**Nature and Survival**. When you travel in the wild, your skill in herbalism makes it easier to identify plants and spot sources of food that others might overlook.
:
**Identify Plants**. You can identify most plants with a quick inspection of their appearance and smell.
:
**Other Activities**
| Activity | DC |
|:---------|---:|
| Find plants | 15 |
| Identify poison | 20 |
| Create salve to remove condition | 20 |

# Chapter VII: Magic and Spellcasting

In many settings, magic permeates the world. It shapes not only the narrative of any given campaign, but also the world itself. The following chapter will discuss both the rules surrounding spell casting, as well as general information regarding spells.

## Spell Rules

A spell is a specific magic effect, bounded by the rules set forth in this chapter and the rules given for the specific spell as well. One should not confuse *magical features* with spells - the two can appear to be completely identical, but are bounded by a different set of rules.

### Armor

In order to cast while wearing armor, a caster must be Trained in the type of armor they are wearing. Otherwi

### Casting Time

All spells have a casting time. Most spells are an action to cast, but some have a different casting time. Some of the more common casting times are as follow:

 - Action
 - Bonus Action
 - Part of an Attack (action)
 - Part of Movement
 - Reaction
 - 1 minute
:
When casting, you must complete the casting uninterrupted before the spell effects occur. Generally speaking, for spells that take an action or less to cast, one will not be interrupted.

### Casting Range

All spells have a range to their effects. Some are miniscule, effectively only making oneself a target for the spell. Others have massive ranges, allowing a caster to target something miles away.

### Components

In order to access the magic needed to cast a spell, different components may be needed.

#### Material (M)

Some spells require physical objects in order to be cast. The items generally are not valuables, but random objects that one may find laying around, or out in nature. These objects are then consumed by the spell. Due to this requirement, many casters carry around component pouches, holding the items they require for casting.

##### Spellcasting Focus

Some spellcasters do not carry around component pouches. Instead, they have a spellcasting focus, which takes the place of material components that do not have a cost associated with them. Spellcasting focuses are magical objects, typically in the form of an amulet or another piece of jewelry.
:
Some spellcastings use spellcasting foci better fitting to their surroundings - wizards tend to use their spellbook as a spellcasting focus, and clerics, their holy book.

#### Somatic (S)

Other spells require specific hand motions to be cast. Without the movement, the spell effects do not occur. This does mean that a caster who is Grappled or Restrained cannot cast spells with a Somatic requirement.

#### Verbal (V)

Finally, some spells require the uttering of magical words. Spells with a verbal component cannot be cast if a character cannot make the sounds to fulfill the requirement.

### Duration

The effects of a spell can last a variable amount of time. Unless otherwise specified, it is assumumed a spell is instantaneous

#### Concentration

Some spells require the caster to concentrate on the spell effects. These spells have a maximum duration defined before a caster's concentration is broken. The caster can choose to break concentration earlier as part of any other action.
:
While the effects of a concentration spell are active, a caster cannot cast another concentration spell without breaking the existing concentration. Likewise, if a caster is knocked unconscious or killed, they lose concentration.
:
For every instance of damage taken while cocentrating on a spell, a caster must make a Mental Fortitude Saving Throw against a DC of the damage taken. If they fail, they lose concentration.

#### Instantaneous

An instantaneous spell is cast, it's effects are instantly applied, and the spell is done. The magic from the spell only exists the moment the spellcasting finishes.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VII: Magic and Spellcasting | Spell Rules }}

\page

### Mana

All spells have a set mana amount. You must have enough mana in order to cast a spell. Once a spell is cast, you expend the required amount of mana.

### Targets

A spell may have a specific set of items and creatures you can target. In order to target a creature fitting the requirements, they must be within the spell's range, you must be able to see the creature and have an unobstructed path to the target.

#### Area of Effect (AOE)

Some spells cause AOE effects, allowing them to hit multiple targets within the range of the AOE. Spells that cause these types of effects have a shape defining the tiles affected, as well as a point of origin, which is where the effect starts.
:
AOE effects are generally blocked by full cover, such a wall, but tend to go through half cover, such as a bush.

##### Cone

A cone extends in a direction you choose from its point of origin. The point of origin must be within range of the spell, and the cone extends to the range of the spell. If the spell dictates a size of the cone, only point of origin must be within the range of the spell.
:
Unless otherwise specified, the cone's angle is 45°. If a square is at least half-way covered by the cone, it is considered within the area of the cone.

##### Line

A line extends from the point of origin to the range of the spell, assuming it doesn't hit an object that would be considered full cover. The point of origin does not need to be the caster, and can be anywhere within range of the spell.

##### Sphere

The point of origin of a sphere is the exact center. If the sphere does not have a specified size, the point of origin must be yourself, and the spell extends out to the range of the spell.
:
If the sphere does have a size, the point of origin must be within the range of the spell, but the entire sphere does not need to be within range.

##### Star

The point of origin of a star is the exact center, where the spell is targetting. From here, the target radiates out by the radius defined in all 8 directions, in straight lines.
:
Any creature falling on the line within the radius defined by the spell is hit.

## Casting a Spell

Now that the rules and requirements in order to cast a spell have been described, the following are rules regarding what happens when a spell is actually cast.

### Attack Roll vs Saving Throw

Many spells will require an attack roll, a Saving Throw or both. If either are required, the spell will dictate which is needed, as well as the DC to pass it.
:
The attack rolls of spells are calculated as 1d20 + your modifier for the school of magic. The spell will dictate if it's a melee or ranged attack. These attacks follow the standard attack rules as outlined in Chapter IX. 
:
Spells that require a Saving Throw by their target will have a specified DC to beat. Generally, the DC will be your spellcasting DC, which is 10 + your spellcasting for the school of magic.

### Overlapping Effects

Many spells have similar, or even the same, effects as another spell. If a character is affected by two spells giving them the same effects (the strength of the effects can vary), the will only be affected by the more potent of the two effects.

## Schools of Magic

It is believed that all magic falls into one of the below schools. Each school has its own unqiue properties, which binds each spell within the school together.

### Abjuration

Abjuration spells are protective in nature, although they can be used aggressively. The create magical barriers, negate harmful effects, harm trespassers or banish creatures to other planes of existence. This school tends to hold all blessings.

### Conjuration

Conjuration spells transport and summon objects from one location to another. Some spells transports objects from one place to another, while others summon objects out of thin air.

### Divination

Divination spells reveal information, whether in the form of secrets long forgotten, glimpses of the future, the locations of hidden things, the truth behind illusions, or visions of distant people or places.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VII: Magic and Spellcasting | Casting A Spell }}

\page

### Enchantment

Enchantment spells affect the minds of others, influencing or controlling their behavior. Such spells can make enemies see the caster as a freid, force creatures to take a course of action, or even control another creature like a puppet.
:
Those who generally use enchantment face the fear and ire of others. If the schools of magic were to be rated on a good-evil scale, Enchantment magic would be rated as the most evil.

### Evocation

Evocation spells manipuate magic to produce an effect. These effects generally are deadly.

### Illusion

Illusion spells deceive the sense or minds of others. They cause people to see things that are not there, to miss things that are there, to hear phantom noises, or the remember things that never happened. Some illusions create phantom images that any creature can see, but the most insidious illusions plant an image directly in the mind of a creature.

### Malediction

Malediction spells curse others. They cause people to grow weak, unable to defend themselves.

### Necromancy

Necromancy spells manipulate the energies of life and death. Such spells can grant an extra reserve of life force, drain the life from another craeture, create the undead, or even bring the dead back to life.

### Transmutation

Transmutation sdpells change the properties of a creature, object or environment. They might turn an enemy into a harmless creature, bolster the strength of an ally, make an object move at the caster's command, or enhance a creature's innate healing abilities to rapidly recover from an injury.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VII: Magic and Spellcasting | Casting A Spell }}

\page

## Spells

### Level 1

#### Absorb Elements
*1st-level transmutation*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Reaction
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: S
**Duration:**     												:: 1 Round
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard
**Potential Damage Types:**								:: Acid, Cold, Fire, Lightning, Poison

You can use this reaction when you are hit with Acid, Cold, Lightning, Fire or Poison damage. The spell captures some of the incoming energy, lessening its effect on you and storing it for your next melee attack. You have resistance to the triggering damage type until the start of your next turn. Also, the first time you hit with a melee attack on your next turn, the target takes an extra 1d6 damage of the triggering type, and the spell ends.

#### Acid Splash
*1st-level conjuration*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 60 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V
**Duration:**     												:: Instantaneous
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard
**Potential Damage Types:**								:: Acid

You hurl a bubble of acid. Choose one creature you can see within range. The creature must succeed on a Reflex or Constitution Saving Throw or take 1d6 acid damage.

#### Alarm
*1st-level abjuration*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Minute
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 30 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a tiny bell and a piece of fine silver wire)
**Duration:**     												:: 8 Hours
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Druid, Wizard

You set an alarm against unwanted intrusion. Choose a door, a window, or an area within range that is no larger than a 20-foot cube. Until the spell ends, an alarm alerts you whenever a Tiny or larger creature touches or enters the warded area. When you cast the spell, you can designate creatures that won't set off the alarm. You also choose whether the alarm is mental or audible.
:
A mental alarm alerts you with a ping in your mind if you are within 1 mile of the warded area. This ping awakens you if you are sleeping.
:
An audible alarm produces the sound of a hand bell for 10 seconds within 60 feet.

#### Animal Friendship
*1st-level enchantment*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 30 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a morsel of food)
**Duration:**     												:: 24 Hours
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Druid

This spell lets you convince a beast that you mean it no harm. Choose a beast that you can see within range. It must see and hear you. If the beast's Intelligence is 4 or higher, the spell fails. Otherwise, the beast must succeed on a Mental Fortitude Saving Throw or be charmed by you for the spell's duration. If you or one of your companions harms the target, the spell ends.

#### Bane
*1st-level enchantment*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 30 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a drop of blood)
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 1 Minute
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Bard, Wizard

A target within range must make a Mental Fortitude Saving Throw. Upon a failure, whenever the target makes an attack roll or a saving throw before the spell ends, the target must roll a d4 and subtract the number rolled from the attack roll or saving throw.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VII: Magic and Spellcasting | Casting A Spell }}

\page

#### Beast Bond
*1st-level divination*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Touch
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a bit of fur wrapped in a cloth)
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 10 Minutes
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Druid, Wizard

You establish a telepathic link with one beast you touch that is friendly to you or charmed by you. The spell fails if the beast's Intelligence score is 4 or higher. Until the spell ends, the link is active while you and the beast are within line of sight of each other. Through the link, the beast can understand your telepathic messages to it, and it can telepathically communicate simple emotions and concepts back to you. While the link is active, the beast gains advantage on attack rolls against any creature within 5 feet of you that you can see.

#### Bless
*1st-level enchantment*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 30 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a sprinkling of holy water)
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 1 Minute
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Cleric, Wizard

You bless one creatures of your choice within range. Whenever that target makes an attack roll or a saving throw before the spell ends, the target can roll a d4 and add the number rolled to the attack roll or saving throw.

#### Blink
*1st-level conjuration*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Ability Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: S
**Duration:**     												:: Instantaneous
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Bard, Cleric, Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard

Choose an unoccupied square within your remaining movement speed that you can see. You blink while imagining yourself in this location, and when you open them, you find yourself in that square. The distance between your original location and your current location is counted against your movement for this round.

#### Burning Touch
*1st-level evocation*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Touch
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: Instantaneous
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer
**Potential Damage Types:**								:: Fire

Make a melee spell attack against a creature you can touch. Upon a hit, the target takes 1d8 fire damage. If the creature is a construct, it instead regains a number of hit points equal to 1d8 + your Evocation Spellcasting Modifier.

#### Ceremony
*1st-level abjuration*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Hour
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Touch
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (25 gp worth of powdered silver, which the spell consumes)
**Duration:**     												:: Instantaneous
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Cleric

You perform a special religious ceremony that is infused with magic. When you cast the spell, choose one of the following rites, the target of which must be within 10 feet of you throughout the casting.
:
Atonement. You touch one willing creature whose alignment has changed, and you make a DC 20 Wisdom (Insight) check. On a successful check, you restore the target to its original alignment.
:
Bless Water. You touch one vial of water and cause it to become holy water.
:
Coming of Age. You touch one humanoid who is a young adult. For the next 24 hours, whenever the target makes an ability check, it can roll a d4 and add the number rolled to the ability check. A creature can benefit from this rite only once.
:
Dedication. You touch one humanoid who wishes to be dedicated to your god's service. For the next 24 hours, whenever the target makes a saving throw, it can roll a d4 and add the number rolled to the save. A creature can benefit from this rite only once.
:
Funeral Rite. You touch one corpse, and for the next 7 days, the target can't become undead by any means short of a wish spell.
:
Wedding. You touch adult humanoids willing to be bonded together in marriage. For the next 7 days, each target gains a +2 bonus to AC while they are within 30 feet of each other. A creature can benefit from this rite again only if widowed.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VII: Magic and Spellcasting | Casting A Spell }}

\page

#### Charm Person
*1st-level enchantment*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 30 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: 1 Hour
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Bard, Sorcerer, Wizard

You attempt to charm a humanoid you can see within range. It must make a Mental Fortitude Saving Throw, and does so with advantage if you or your companions are fighting it. If it fails the saving throw, it is charmed by you until the spell ends or until you or your companions do anything harmful to it. The charmed creature regards you as a friendly acquaintance. When the spell ends, the creature knows it was charmed by you.

#### Color Spray
*1st-level illusion*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a pinch of powder or sand that is colored red, yellow, and blue)
**Duration:**     												:: 1 Round
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Sorcerer, Wizard

A dazzling array of flashing, colored light springs from your hand. Roll 6d10; the total is how many hit points of creatures this spell can effect. Creatures in a 15-foot cone originating from you are affected in ascending order of their current hit points (ignoring unconscious creatures and creatures that can't see).
:
Starting with the creature that has the lowest current hit points, each creature affected by this spell is blinded until the end of your next turn. Subtract each creature's hit points from the total before moving on to the creature with the next lowest hit points. A creature's hit points must be equal to or less than the remaining total for that creature to be affected.

#### Command
*1st-level enchantment*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 60 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V
**Duration:**     												:: 1 Round
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Bard, Sorcerer, Wizard

You speak a one-word command to a creature you can see within range. The target must succeed on a Mental Fortitude Saving Throw or follow the command on its next turn. The spell has no effect if the target is undead, if it doesn't understand your language, or if your command is directly harmful to it.
:
Some typical commands and their effects follow. You might issue a command other than one described here. If you do so, the DM determines how the target behaves. If the target can't follow your command, the spell ends.
:
Approach. The target moves toward you by the shortest and most direct route, ending its turn if it moves within 5 feet of you.
:
Drop. The target drops whatever it is holding and then ends its turn.
:
Flee. The target spends its turn moving away from you by the fastest available means.
:
Grovel. The target falls prone and then ends its turn.
:
Halt. The target doesn't move and takes no actions. A flying creature stays aloft, provided that it is able to do so. If it must move to stay aloft, it flies the minimum distance needed to remain in the air.

#### Comprehend Languages
*1st-level divination*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a pinch of soot and salt)
**Duration:**     												:: 1 Hour
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Bard, Sorcerer, Wizard

For the duration, you understand the literal meaning of any spoken language that you hear. You also understand any written language that you see, but you must be touching the surface on which the words are written. It takes about 1 minute to read one page of text.
:
This spell doesn't decode secret messages in a text or a glyph, such as an arcane sigil, that isn't part of a written language.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VII: Magic and Spellcasting | Casting A Spell }}

\page

#### Control Flames
*1st-level transmutation*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 60 Feet
**Components:**   												:: S
**Duration:**     												:: Instantaneous or 1 Hour (see below)
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard

You choose nonmagical flame that you can see within range and that fits within a 5-foot cube. You affect it in one of the following ways:
:
 - You instantaneously expand the flame 5 feet in one direction, provided that wood or other fuel is present in the new location.
:
 - You instantaneously extinguish the flames within the cube.
:
 - You double or halve the area of bright light and dim light cast by the flame, change its color, or both. The change lasts for 1 hour.
:
 - You cause simple shapes—such as the vague form of a creature, an inanimate object, or a location—to appear within the flames and animate as you like. The shapes last for 1 hour.

#### Counterspell
*1st-level abjuration*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Reaction
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 60 Feet
**Components:**   												:: S
**Duration:**     												:: Instantaneous
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Sorcerer, Wizard

You attempt to disrupt the casting of a spell. Although this spell is technically a level 1 spell, it can be cast at any level, assuming you can cast spells at that level as well.
:
If the spell is if the level Counterspell is cast at or lower, you automatically disrupt the spell. Otherwise, the caster of the original spell must make an Arcana Saving Throw against your Abjuration Spell Save DC.

#### Cure Wounds
*1st-level necromancy*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Touch
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: Instantaneous
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Bard, Cleric, Druid

A creature you touch regains a number of hit points equal to 1d8 + your Necromancy Spellcasting Modifier. This spell has no effect on undead or constructs.

#### Detect Good and Evil
*1st-level divination*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 10 Minutes
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Cleric, Druid

For the duration, you know if there is an aberration, celestial, elemental, fey, fiend, or undead within 30 feet of you, as well as where the creature is located. Similarly, you know if there is a place or object within 30 feet of you that has been magically consecrated or desecrated.
:
The spell can penetrate most barriers, but it is blocked by 1 foot of stone, 1 inch of common metal, a thin sheet of lead, or 3 feet of wood or dirt.

#### Detect Magic
*1st-level divination*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 10 Minutes
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Bard, Cleric, Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard

For the duration, you sense the presence of magic within 30 feet of you. If you sense magic in this way, you can use your action to see a faint aura around any visible creature or object in the area that bears magic, and you learn its school of magic, if any.
:
The spell can penetrate most barriers, but it is blocked by 1 foot of stone, 1 inch of common metal, a thin sheet of lead, or 3 feet of wood or dirt.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VII: Magic and Spellcasting | Casting A Spell }}

\page

#### Detect Poison and Disease
*1st-level divination*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a yew leaf)
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 10 Minutes
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Cleric, Druid

For the duration, you can sense the presence and location of poisons, poisonous creatures, and diseases within 30 feet of you. You also identify the kind of poison, poisonous creature, or disease in each case.
:
The spell can penetrate most barriers, but it is blocked by 1 foot of stone, 1 inch of common metal, a thin sheet of lead, or 3 feet of wood or dirt.

#### Disguise Self
*1st-level illusion*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: 1 Hour
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Bard, Wizard

You make yourself—including your clothing, armor, weapons, and other belongings on your person—look different until the spell ends or until you use your action to dismiss it. You can seem 1 foot shorter or taller and can appear thin, fat, or in between. You can't change your body type, so you must adopt a form that has the same basic arrangement of limbs. Otherwise, the extent of the illusion is up to you.
:
The changes wrought by this spell fail to hold up to physical inspection. For example, if you use this spell to add a hat to your outfit, objects pass through the hat, and anyone who touches it would feel nothing or would feel your head and hair. If you use this spell to appear thinner than you are, the hand of someone who reaches out to touch you would bump into you while it was seemingly still in midair.
:
To discern that you are disguised, a creature can use its action to inspect your appearance and must succeed on an Investigation check against your Illusion Spell Save DC.

#### Dispel Magic
*1st-level abjuration*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 120 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: Instantaneous
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Bard, Cleric, Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard

At your touch, one magical effect (not a curse - see Remove Curse) affecting a creature or object is cured. Although this spell is technically a level 1 spell, it can be cast at any level, assuming you can cast spells at that level as well.
:
If the effect of a higher level than this spell is cast, you must roll a d20 and add your Abjuration Spellcasting Modifier against a DC of 10 + the normal casting amount of one level lower than the effect's level, rounded up. For instance, a magical effect cast by a level 5 spell would have a DC of 18 (10 + 8 [the 8 comes from the standard 8 mana used to cast a level 4 spell]).
:
Dispel Magic cast at the sixth level will always remove the targetted effect.

#### Distort Value
*1st-level illusion*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Hour
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Touch
**Components:**   												:: V
**Duration:**     												:: 8 Hours
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Sorcerer, Wizard

You cast this spell on an object no more than 1 foot on a side, doubling the object's perceived value by adding illusory flourishes or polish to it, or reducing its perceived value by half with the help of illusory scratches, dents, and other unsightly features. Anyone examining the object can ascertain its true value with a successful Investigation Check against your Illusion Spell Save DC.

#### Divine Favor
*1st-level evocation*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Ability Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a melee weapon)
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 1 Minute
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Cleric
**Potential Damage Types:**								:: Radiant

Your prayer empowers you with divine radiance. Make a melee weapon attack. You deal an extra 1d4 radiant damage on a hit.

{{pageNumber,auto}}
{{footnote Chapter VII: Magic and Spellcasting | Casting A Spell }}

\page

#### Entangle
*1st-level conjuration*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 90 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 1 Minute
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Druid

Grasping weeds and vines sprout from the ground in a 20-foot square starting from a point within range. For the duration, these plants turn the ground in the area into difficult terrain.
:
A creature in the area when you cast the spell must succeed on an Athletics or Reflex Saving Throw or be restrained by the entangling plants until the spell ends. A creature restrained by the plants can use its action to make an Athletics Check against your Conjuration Spell Save DC. On a success, it frees itself.
:
When the spell ends, the conjured plants wilt away.

#### Expeditious Retreat
*1st-level transmutation*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Ability Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Touch
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 10 Minutes
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Wizard

This spell allows you to move at an incredible pace. When you cast this spell, and then as a Ability Action on each of your turns until the spell ends, you can take the Dash action.

#### False Life
*1st-level necromancy*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: Self
**Components:**   												:: V,S,M (a small amount of alcohol or distilled spirits)
**Duration:**     												:: 1 Hour
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Bard, Cleric

Bolstering yourself with a necromantic facsimile of life, you gain 1d4 + 4 temporary hit points for the duration.

#### Fear
*1st-level malediction*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 60 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 1 Minute
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard

You awaken the sense of mortality in one creature you can see within range. A construct or an undead is immune to this effect. The target must succeed on a Mental Fortitude or Insight Saving Throw or become frightened of you until the spell ends. Upon a failure, the creature gains the Frightened I condition.
:
The frightened target can repeat the saving throw at the end of each of its turns, ending the effect on itself on a success.

#### Fire Bolt
*1st-level evocation*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 120 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: Instantaneous
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Artificer, Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard
**Potential Damage Types:**								:: Fire

You hurl a mote of fire at a creature or object within range. Make a ranged spell attack against the target. On a hit, the target takes 1d10 fire damage. A flammable object hit by this spell ignites if it isn't being worn or carried.

#### Fog Cloud
*1st-level conjuration*

**Casting Time:** 												:: 1 Action
**Mana Cost:**														:: 2 mana
**Range:**        												:: 120 Feet
**Components:**   												:: V,S
**Duration:**     												:: Concentration, up to 1 Hour
**Magic Archetype Implementations:**			:: Druid, Sorcerer, Wizard

You create a 20-foot-radius sphere of fog centered on a point within range. The sphere spreads around corners, and its area is heavily obscured. Any creature within the fog is Blinded, and provides cover from any attack, assuming the attacker also cannot see through the fog. It lasts for the duration or until a wind of moderate or greater speed (at least 10 miles per hour) disperses it.
